Remark 6.2.5. A sign to look beyond the symmetric local lemma is when there are

bad events of very different nature (e.g., having very different probabilities).

Compactness argument
Now we highlight an important compactness argument that allows us to deduce the
existence of an infinite object, even though the local lemma itself is only applicable to
finite systems.
Theorem 6.2.6

Let рқҗ» be a (non-uniform) hypergraph on a possibly infinite vertex set, such that
each edge is finite, has at least рқ‘ҳ vertices, and intersect at most рқ‘‘ other edges. If
рқ‘’2вҲ’рқ‘ҳ+1 (рқ‘‘ + 1) вүӨ 1, then рқҗ» has a proper 2-coloring.
Proof. From a vanilla application of the symmetric local lemma, we deduce that for

any finite subset рқ‘Ӣ of vertices, there exists an 2-coloring рқ‘Ӣ so that no edge contained
in рқ‘Ӣ is monochromatic (color each vertex iid uniformly, and consider the bad event рқҗҙрқ‘’
that the edge рқ‘’ вҠҶ рқ‘Ӣ is monochromatic).
Next we extend the coloring to the entire vertex set рқ‘ү by a compactness argument. The
set of all colorings is [2] рқ‘ү . By TikhonovвҖҷs theorem (which says a product of a possibly

84

6.2 Coloring hypergraphs
infinite collection of compact topological spaces is compact), [2] рқ‘ү is compact under
the product topology.
For each finite subset рқ‘Ӣ, let рқҗ¶ рқ‘Ӣ вҠҶ [2] рқ‘ү be the subset of colorings where no edge
contained in рқ‘Ӣ is monochromatic. Earlier from the local lemma we saw that рқҗ¶ рқ‘Ӣ вү  вҲ….
If рқ‘Ң вҠҶ рқ‘Ӣ, then рқҗ¶рқ‘Ң вҠҮ рқҗ¶ рқ‘Ӣ . Thus
рқҗ¶ рқ‘Ӣ1 вҲ© В· В· В· вҲ© рқҗ¶ рқ‘Ӣв„“ вҠҮ рқҗ¶ рқ‘Ӣ1 вҲӘВ·В·В·вҲӘрқ‘Ӣв„“ ,
so {рқҗ¶ рқ‘Ӣ : |рқ‘Ӣ | < вҲһ} is a collection of closed subsets of [2] рқ‘ү with the finite intersection
property (i.e., the intersection of any finite subcollection is nonempty).
Recall from point-set topology the following basic fact (a defining property): a space
is compact if and only if every family of closed subsets having the finite intersection
property has non-empty intersection.
Hence by compactness of [2] рқ‘ү , the intersection of рқҗ¶ рқ‘Ӣ taken over all finite рқ‘Ӣ is
non-empty. Any element of this intersection corresponds to a valid coloring of the
hypergraph.
в–Ў
More generally, the above compactness argument yields the following.
Lemma 6.2.7 (Compactness argument)

Consider a variation of the random variable model (Setup 6.1.5) where each variable
has only finitely many choices but there can be possibly infinitely many events (each
event depends on a finite subset of variables). If it is possible to avoid any finite subset
of events, then it is possible to avoid all the events.
в–Ў
Remark 6.2.8. Note the conclusion may be false if we do not assume the random
variable model (why?).

The next application appears in the paper of ErdЕ‘s and LovГЎsz (1975) where the local
lemma originally appears.
Consider рқ‘ҳ-coloring the real numbers, i.e., a function рқ‘җ : R вҶ’ [рқ‘ҳ]. We say that рқ‘Ү вҠҶ R
is multicolored with respect to рқ‘җ if all рқ‘ҳ colors appear in рқ‘Ү.
Question 6.2.9

For each рқ‘ҳ is there an рқ‘ҡ so that for every рқ‘Ҷ вҠҶ R with |рқ‘Ҷ| = рқ‘ҡ, one can рқ‘ҳ-color R so
that every translate of рқ‘Ҷ is multicolored?
The following theorem shows that this can be done whenever рқ‘ҡ > (3 + рқңҖ)рқ‘ҳ log рқ‘ҳ and
рқ‘ҳ > рқ‘ҳ 0 (рқңҖ) sufficiently large.

6 LovГЎsz Local Lemma

Theorem 6.2.10

The answer to the above equation is yes if

Proof. Each translate of рқ‘Ҷ is not multicolored with probability рқ‘қ вүӨ рқ‘ҳ (1 вҲ’ 1/рқ‘ҳ) рқ‘ҡ , and

each translate of рқ‘Ҷ intersects at most рқ‘ҡ(рқ‘ҡ вҲ’ 1) other translates. Consider a bad event

is possible to avoid all the bad events.

Decomposing coverings
We say that a collection of disks in Rрқ‘‘ is a covering if their union is Rрқ‘‘ . We say that
it is a рқ’Ң-fold covering if every point of Rрқ‘‘ is contained in at least рқ‘ҳ disks (so 1-fold
covering is the same as a covering).
We say that a рқ‘ҳ-fold covering is decomposable if it can be partitioned into two coverings.
In Rрқ‘‘ , is a every рқ‘ҳ-fold covering by unit balls decomposable if рқ‘ҳ is sufficiently large?
A fun exercise: in R1 , every рқ‘ҳ-fold covering by intervals can be partitioned into рқ‘ҳ
coverings.
Mani-Levitska and Pach (1986) showed that every 33-fold covering of R2 is decomposable.
What about higher dimensions?
Surprising, they also showed that for every рқ‘ҳ, there exists a рқ‘ҳ-fold indecomposable
covering of R3 (and similarly for Rрқ‘‘ for рқ‘‘ вүҘ 3).
However, it turns out that indecomposable coverings must cover the space quite unevenly:

87

6 LovГЎsz Local Lemma

Theorem 6.2.12 (Mani-Levitska and Pach 1986)

Every рқ‘ҳ-fold nondecomposable covering of R3 by open unit balls must cover some
point вүі 2 рқ‘ҳ/3 times.
Remark 6.2.13. In Rрқ‘‘ , the same proof gives вүҘ рқ‘җ рқ‘‘ 2 рқ‘ҳ/рқ‘‘ .

We will need the following combinatorial geometric fact:
Lemma 6.2.14

A set of рқ‘ӣ вүҘ 2 spheres in R3 cut R3 into at most рқ‘ӣ3 connected components.
Proof. Let us first consider the problem in one dimension lower. Let рқ‘“ (рқ‘ҡ) be the

maximum number of connected regions that рқ‘ҡ circles on a sphere in R3 can cut the
sphere into.
We have рқ‘“ (рқ‘ҡ + 1) вүӨ рқ‘“ (рқ‘ҡ) + 2рқ‘ҡ for all рқ‘ҡ вүҘ 1 since adding a new circle to a set of рқ‘ҡ
circles creates at most 2рқ‘ҡ intersection points, so that the new circle is divided into at
most 2рқ‘ҡ arcs, and hence its addition creates at most 2рқ‘ҡ new regions.
Combined with рқ‘“ (1) = 2, we deduce рқ‘“ (рқ‘ҡ) вүӨ рқ‘ҡ(рқ‘ҡ вҲ’ 1) + 2 for all рқ‘ҡ вүҘ 1.
Now let рқ‘”(рқ‘ҡ) be the maximum number of connected regions that рқ‘ҡ spheres in R3 can
cut R3 into. We have рқ‘”(1) = 2, and рқ‘”(рқ‘ҡ + 1) вүӨ рқ‘”(рқ‘ҡ) + рқ‘“ (рқ‘ҡ) вүӨ рқ‘”(рқ‘ҡ) by a similar
argument as earlier. So рқ‘”(рқ‘ҡ) вүӨ рқ‘“ (рқ‘ҡ вҲ’ 1) + рқ‘“ (рқ‘ҡ вҲ’ 2) + В· В· В· + рқ‘“ (1) + рқ‘”(0) вүӨ рқ‘ҡ 3 . в–Ў
Proof. Suppose for contradiction that every point in R3 is covered by at most рқ‘Ў вүӨ рқ‘җ2 рқ‘ҳ/3

unit balls from рқҗ№ (for some sufficiently small рқ‘җ that we will pick later).
Construct an infinite hypergraph рқҗ» with vertex set being the set of balls and edges
having the form рқҗё рқ‘Ҙ = {balls containing рқ‘Ҙ} for some рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ R3 . Note that |рқҗё рқ‘Ҙ | вүҘ рқ‘ҳ since
we have a рқ‘ҳ-fold covering.
Also, note that if рқ‘Ҙ, рқ‘Ұ вҲҲ R3 lie in the same connected component in the complement of
the union of all the unit spheres, then рқҗё рқ‘Ҙ = рқҗё рқ‘Ұ (i.e., the same edge).
Claim: every edge of intersects at most рқ‘‘ = рқ‘Ӯ (рқ‘Ў 3 ) other edges
Proof of claim: Let рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ R3 . If рқҗё рқ‘Ҙ вҲ© рқҗё рқ‘Ұ вү  вҲ…, then |рқ‘Ҙ вҲ’ рқ‘Ұ| вүӨ 2, so all the balls in
рқҗё рқ‘Ұ lie in the radius-4 ball centered at рқ‘Ҙ. The volume of the radius-4 ball is 43 times
the unit ball. Since every point lies in at most рқ‘Ў balls, there are at most 43 рқ‘Ў balls
appearing among those рқҗё рқ‘Ұ intersecting рқ‘Ҙ, and these balls cut the radius-2 centered at
рқ‘Ҙ into рқ‘Ӯ (рқ‘Ў 3 ) connected regions by the earlier lemma, and two different рқ‘ҰвҖҷs in the same
region produce the same рқҗё рқ‘Ұ . So рқҗё рқ‘Ҙ intersects рқ‘Ӯ (рқ‘Ў 3 ) other edges. в– 

88

6.3 Independent transversal
With рқ‘Ў вүӨ рқ‘җ2 рқ‘ҳ/3 and рқ‘җ sufficiently small, and knowing рқ‘‘ = рқ‘Ӯ (рқ‘Ў 3 ) from the claim, we
have рқ‘’2вҲ’рқ‘ҳ+1 (рқ‘‘ + 1) вүӨ 1. It then follows by Theorem 6.2.6 (local lemma + compactness
argument) that this hypergraph is 2-colorable, which corresponds to a decomposition
of the covering, a contradiction.
в–Ў

6.3 Independent transversal
The application of the local lemma in this section is instructive in that it is not obvious
at first what to choose as bad events (even if you are already told to apply the local
lemma). It is worth trying different possibilities.
Every graph with maximum degree О” contains an independent set of size вүҘ |рқ‘ү |/(О”+1)
(choose the independent set greedily). The following lemma shows that by decreasing
the desired size of the independent set by a constant factor, we can guarantee an
independent set that is also a transversal to a vertex set partition.
Theorem 6.3.1

Let рқҗә = (рқ‘ү, рқҗё) be a graph with maximum degree О” and let рқ‘ү = рқ‘ү1 вҲӘ В· В· В· вҲӘ рқ‘үрқ‘ҹ be a
partition, where each |рқ‘үрқ‘– | вүҘ 2рқ‘’О”. Then there is an independent set in рқҗә containing
one vertex from each рқ‘үрқ‘– .
Proof. The first step in the proof is simple yet subtle: we may assume that |рқ‘үрқ‘– | = рқ‘ҳ :=

вҢҲ2рқ‘’О”вҢү for each рқ‘–, or else we can remove some vertices from рқ‘үрқ‘– (if we do not trim the
vertex sets now, we will run into difficulties later).
Pick рқ‘Ј рқ‘– вҲҲ рқ‘үрқ‘– uniformly at random, independently for each рқ‘–.
This is an instance of the random variable model (Setup 6.1.5), where рқ‘Ј 1 , . . . , рқ‘Ј рқ‘ҹ are
the random variables.
We would like to design a collection of вҖңbad eventsвҖқ so that if we avoid all of them,
then {рқ‘Ј 1 , . . . , рқ‘Ј рқ‘ҹ } is guaranteed to be independent set.
What do we choose as bad events? It turns out that some choices work better than
others.
Attempt 1:
For each 1 вүӨ рқ‘– < рқ‘— вүӨ рқ‘ҹ where there exists an edge between рқ‘үрқ‘– and рқ‘ү рқ‘— , let рқҗҙрқ‘–, рқ‘— be the
event that рқ‘Ј рқ‘– is adjacent to рқ‘Ј рқ‘— .
We find that P( рқҗҙрқ‘–, рқ‘— ) вүӨ О”/рқ‘ҳ.
The canonical dependency graph has рқҗҙрқ‘–, рқ‘— вҲј рқҗҙрқ‘– вҖІ , рқ‘— вҖІ if and only if the two sets {рқ‘–, рқ‘— } and
{рқ‘–вҖІ, рқ‘— вҖІ } intersect. This dependency graph has max degree вүӨ 2О”рқ‘ҳ (starting from (рқ‘–, рқ‘—),

89

6 LovГЎsz Local Lemma
look at the neighbors of all vertices in рқ‘үрқ‘– вҲӘ рқ‘ү рқ‘— ). The max degree is too large compared
to the bad event probabilities.
Attempt 2:
For each edge рқ‘’ вҲҲ рқҗё, let рқҗҙрқ‘’ be the event that both endpoints of рқ‘’ are picked.
We have P( рқҗҙрқ‘’ ) = 1/рқ‘ҳ 2 .
The canonical dependency graph has рқҗҙрқ‘’ вҲј рқҗҙ рқ‘“ if some рқ‘үрқ‘– intersects both рқ‘’ and рқ‘“ .
This dependency graph has max degree вүӨ 2рқ‘ҳО” (if рқ‘’ is between рқ‘үрқ‘– and рқ‘ү рқ‘— , then рқ‘“ must
be incident to рқ‘үрқ‘– вҲӘ рқ‘ү рқ‘— ).
We have рқ‘’(1/рқ‘ҳ 2 )(2рқ‘ҳО” + 1) вүӨ 1, so the local lemma implies the with probability no
bad event occurs, in which case {рқ‘Ј 1 , . . . , рқ‘Ј рқ‘ҹ } is an independent set.
в–Ў
Remark 6.3.2. Alon (1988) introduced the above result as lemma in his near resolution

of the still-open linear arboricity conjecture (see the AlonвҖ“Spencer textbook В§5.5).
AlonвҖҷs approach makes heavy use of the local lemma.
Haxell (1995, 2001) relaxed the hypothesis to |рқ‘үрқ‘– | вүҘ 2О” for each рқ‘–. The statement
becomes false if 2О” is replaced by 2О” вҲ’ 1 (SzabГі and Tardos 2006).

6.4 Directed cycles of length divisible by рқ‘ҳ
A directed graph is рқ’…-regular if every vertex has in-degree рқ‘‘ and out-degree рқ‘‘.
Theorem 6.4.1 (Alon and Linial 1989)

For every рқ‘ҳ there exists рқ‘‘ so that every рқ‘‘-regular directed graph has a directed cycle
of length divisible by рқ‘ҳ.

Corollary 6.4.2

For every рқ‘ҳ there exists рқ‘‘ so that every 2рқ‘‘-regular graph has a cycle of length divisible
by рқ‘ҳ.
Proof. Every 2рқ‘‘-regular graph can be made into a рқ‘‘-regular digraph by orientating its

edges according to an Eulerian tour. And then we can apply the previous theorem. в–Ў
We will prove the following more general statement.

90

6.4 Directed cycles of length divisible by рқ‘ҳ

Theorem 6.4.3 (Alon and Linial 1989)

Every directed graph with min out-degree рқӣҝ and max in-degree О” contains a cycle of
length divisible by рқ‘ҳ вҲҲ N as long as
рқ‘ҳвүӨ

рқӣҝ
.
1 + log(1 + рқӣҝО”)

Proof. By deleting edges, can assume that every vertex has out-degree exactly рқӣҝ.

Assign every vertex рқ‘Ј an element рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘Ј вҲҲ Z/рқ‘ҳZ iid uniformly at random.
We will look for directed cycles where the labels increase by 1 (mod рқ‘ҳ) at each step.
These cycles all have length divisible by рқ‘ҳ.
For each vertex рқ‘Ј, let рқҗҙрқ‘Ј be the event that there is nowhere to go from рқ‘Ј (i.e., if no
outneighbor is labeled рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘Ј + 1 (mod рқ‘ҳ)). We have
P( рқҗҙрқ‘Ј ) = (1 вҲ’ 1/рқ‘ҳ) рқӣҝ вүӨ рқ‘’ вҲ’рқӣҝ/рқ‘ҳ .
Since рқҗҙрқ‘Ј depends only on {рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘Ө : рқ‘Ө вҲҲ {рқ‘Ј} вҲӘ рқ‘Ғ + (рқ‘Ј)}, where рқ‘Ғ + (рқ‘Ј) denotes the outneighbors of рқ‘Ј and рқ‘Ғ вҲ’ (рқ‘Ј) the in-neighbors of рқ‘Ј, the canonical dependency graph
has
рқҗҙрқ‘Ј вҲј рқҗҙрқ‘Ө if {рқ‘Ј} вҲӘ рқ‘Ғ + (рқ‘Ј) intersects {рқ‘Ө} вҲӘ рқ‘Ғ + (рқ‘Ө).
The maximum degree in the dependency graph is at most О” + рқӣҝО” (starting from рқ‘Ј, there
are
(1) at most О” choices stepping backward
(2) рқӣҝ choices stepping forward, and
(3) at most рқӣҝ(О” вҲ’ 1) choices stepping forward and then backward to land somewhere
other than рқ‘Ј).
So an application of the local lemma shows that we are done as long as рқ‘’ 1вҲ’рқӣҝ/рқ‘ҳ (1+О”+рқӣҝО”),
i.e.,
рқ‘ҳ вүӨ рқӣҝ/(1 + log(1 + О” + рқӣҝО”)).
This is almost, but not quite the result (though, for most applications, we would be
perfectly happy with such a bound).
The final trick is to notice that we actually have an even smaller valid dependency
digraph:
рқҗҙрқ‘Ј is independent of all рқҗҙрқ‘Ө where рқ‘Ғ + (рқ‘Ј) is disjoint from рқ‘Ғ + (рқ‘Ө) вҲӘ {рқ‘Ө}.

91

6 LovГЎsz Local Lemma
Indeed, even if we fix the colors of all vertices outside рқ‘Ғ + (рқ‘Ј), the conditional probability that рқҗҙрқ‘Ј is still (1 вҲ’ 1/рқ‘ҳ) рқӣҝ .
The number of рқ‘Ө such that рқ‘Ғ + (рқ‘Ј) intersects рқ‘Ғ + (рқ‘Ө) вҲӘ {рқ‘Ө} is at most рқӣҝО” (no longer
need to consider (1) in the previous count). And we have
рқ‘’ рқ‘қ(рқӣҝО” + 1) вүӨ рқ‘’ 1вҲ’рқӣҝ/рқ‘ҳ (рқӣҝО” + 1) вүӨ 1.
So we are done by the local lemma.

6.5 Lopsided local lemma
Let us move beyond the random variable model, and consider a collection of bad
events in the general setup of the local lemma. Instead of requiring that each event is
independent of its non-neighbors (in the dependency graph), what if we assume that
avoiding some bad events make it easier to avoid some others? Intuitively, it seems
that it would only make it easier to avoid bad events.
We can make this notion precise by re-examining the proof of the local lemma. Where
did we actually use the independence assumption in the hypothesis of the local lemma?
It was in the following step, Equation (6.3):

observation allows us to weaken the independence assumption. Therefore we have the
following theorem, which was used by ErdЕ‘s and Spencer (1991) to give an application
to Latin transversals that we will see shortly.

Like earlier, by setting рқ‘Ҙрқ‘– = 1/(рқ‘‘ + 1), we deduce a symmetric version that is easier to

Corollary 6.5.2 (Lopsided local lemma; symmetric version)

In the previous theorem, if |рқ‘Ғ (рқ‘–)| вүӨ рқ‘‘ and P( рқҗҙрқ‘– ) вүӨ рқ‘қ for every рқ‘– вҲҲ [рқ‘ӣ], and рқ‘’ рқ‘қ(рқ‘‘ +1) вүӨ

The (di)graph where рқ‘Ғ (рқ‘–) is the set of (out-)neighbors of рқ‘– is called a negative dependency (di)graph.
Remark 6.5.3 (Important!). Just as with the usual local lemma, the negative depen-

dency graph is not constructed by simply checking pairs of events.
The hypothesis of Theorem 6.5.1 seems annoying to check. Fortunately, many applications of lopsided local lemma fall within a model that we will soon describe, where
there is a canonical negative dependency graph that is straightforward to construct.
This is analogous to the random variable model for the usual local lemma, where the
canonical dependence graph has two events adjacency if they share variables.

Random injection model
We describe a random injection model where there is an easy-to-construct canonical
negative dependency graph (Lu and SzГ©kely 2007).
Recall that a matching in a graph is a subset of edges with no two sharing a vertex.
In a bipartite graph with vertex parts рқ‘Ӣ and рқ‘Ң , a complete matching from рқ‘Ӣ to рқ‘Ң is a
matching where every vertex of рқ‘Ӣ belongs to an edge of the matching.

93

6 LovГЎsz Local Lemma

Setup 6.5.4 (Random injection model)

Let рқ‘Ӣ and рқ‘Ң be finite sets with |рқ‘Ӣ | вүӨ |рқ‘Ң |.

that рқҗ№ вҠҶ рқ‘Җ.

Latin transversal
A Latin square of order рқ‘ӣ is an рқ‘ӣ Г— рқ‘ӣ array filled with рқ‘ӣ symbols so that every symbol
appears exactly once in every row and column. Example:

These objects are called Latin squares because they were studied by Euler (1707вҖ“1783)
who used Latin symbols to fill the arrays.

Given an рқ‘ӣ Г— рқ‘ӣ array, a transversal is a set of рқ‘ӣ entries with one in every row and
column. A Latin transversal is a transversal with distinct entries. Example:

Here are is a famous open conjecture about Latin transversals.1 (Do you see why the
hypothesis on parity is necessary?)
Conjecture 6.5.8 (Ryser 1967)

Every odd order Latin square has a transversal.
The conjecture should be modified for even order Latin squares.
Conjecture 6.5.9 (Ryser-Brualdi-Stein conjecture)

Every even order Latin square has a transversal containing all but at most one symbol.
Remark 6.5.10. Keevash, Pokrovskiy, Sudakov and Yepremyan (2022) proved that

every order рқ‘ӣ Latin square contains a transversal containing all but рқ‘Ӯ (log рқ‘ӣ/log log рқ‘ӣ)
symbols, improving an earlier bound of рқ‘Ӯ (log2 рқ‘ӣ) by Hatami and Shor (2008).
Recently, Montgomery announced a proof of the conjecture for all sufficiently large
even рқ‘ӣ. The proof uses sophisticated techniques combining the semi-random method
and the absorption method.
The next result is the original application of the lopsided local lemma.
Theorem 6.5.11 (ErdЕ‘s and Spencer 1991)

Every рқ‘ӣГ—рқ‘ӣ array where every entry appears at most рқ‘ӣ/(4рқ‘’) times has a Latin transversal.
Proof. Pick a transversal uniformly at random. This is the same as picking a permuta-

tion рқ‘“ : [рқ‘ӣ] вҶ’ [рқ‘ӣ] uniformly at random. In Setup 6.5.4, the random injection model,
transversals correspond to perfect matchings.
For each pair of equal entries in the array not both lying in the same row or column,
consider the bad event that the transversal contains both entries.
The canonical negative dependency graph is obtained by joining an edge between two
bad events if the four entries involved share some row or column.
1 Not to be confused with another conjecture also known as RyserвҖҷs conjecture concerning an inequality

of RyserвҖҷs 1967 paper.

6.6 Algorithmic local lemma
Consider an instance of a problem in the random variable setting (e.g., рқ‘ҳ-CNF) for
which the local lemma guarantees a solution. Can one find a satisfying assignment
efficiently?
The local lemma tells you that some good configuration exists, but the proof is nonconstructive. The probability that a random sample avoids all the bad events is often
very small (usually exponentially small, e.g., in the case of a set of independent bad
events). It had been an open problem for a long time whether the local lemma can be
made algorithmic.
Moser (2009), during his PhD, achieved a breakthrough by coming up with the first
efficient algorithmic version of the local lemma for finding a satisfying assignment
for рқ‘ҳ-CNF formulas. Moser and Tardos (2010) later extended the algorithm for the
general local lemma in the random variable model.
Remark 6.6.1 (Too hard in general). The MoserвҖ“Tardos algorithm works in the ran-

dom variable model (there are subsequent work that concern other models such as
the random injection model). Some assumption on the model is necessary since the
problem can be computationally hard in general.
For example, let рқ‘һ = 2 рқ‘ҳ , and рқ‘“ : [рқ‘һ] вҶ’ [рқ‘һ] be some fixed bДіection (with an explicit
description and easy to compute). Consider the computational task of inverting рқ‘“ :
given рқ‘Ұ вҲҲ [рқ‘һ], find рқ‘Ҙ such that рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ) = рқ‘Ұ (we would like an algorithm with running
time polynomial in рқ‘ҳ).
If рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ [рқ‘һ] is chosen uniformly, then рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ) вҲҲ [рқ‘һ] is also uniform. For each рқ‘– вҲҲ [рқ‘ҳ], let
рқҗҙрқ‘– be the event that рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ) and рқ‘Ұ disagree on рқ‘–-th bit. Then рқҗҙ1 , . . . , рқҗҙ рқ‘ҳ are independent
events. Also, рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ) = рқ‘Ұ if and only if no event рқҗҙрқ‘– occurs. So a trivial version of the
local lemma (with empty dependency graph) implies the existence of some рқ‘Ҙ such that
рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ) = рқ‘Ұ.

97

6 LovГЎsz Local Lemma
On the other hand, it is believed that there exist functions рқ‘“ that is easy to compute but
hard to invert. Such functions are called one-way functions, and they are a fundamental
building block in cryptography. For example, let рқ‘” be a multiplicative generator of Fрқ‘һ ,
and let рқ‘“ : Fрқ‘һ вҶ’ Fрқ‘һ be given by рқ‘“ (0) = 0 and рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ) = рқ‘” рқ‘Ҙ and for рқ‘Ҙ вү  0. Then inverting
рқ‘“ is the discrete logarithm problem, which is believed to be computationally difficult.
The computational difficulty of this problem is the basis for the security of important
public key cryptography schemes, such as the DiffieвҖ“Hellman key exchange.

MoserвҖ“Tardos algorithm
The algorithm is surprisingly simple.
Algorithm 6.6.2 (MoserвҖ“Tardos вҖңfix-itвҖқ)

input : a set of variables and events in the random variable model
output : an assignment of variables avoiding all bad events
Initialize by setting all variables to arbitrary values;
while there is some violated event do
Pick an arbitrary violated event and uniformly resample its variables;
(We can make the algorithm more precise by specifying a way to pick an вҖңarbitraryвҖқ choice, e.g., the
lexicographically first choice.)

Theorem 6.6.3 (Moser and Tardos 2010)

In Algorithm 6.6.2, letting рқҗҙ1 , . . . , рқҗҙрқ‘ӣ denote the bad events, suppose there are
рқ‘Ҙ 1 , . . . , рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘ӣ вҲҲ [0, 1) such that
Г–
P( рқҗҙрқ‘– ) вүӨ рқ‘Ҙрқ‘–
(1 вҲ’ рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘— ) for all рқ‘– вҲҲ [рқ‘ӣ],
рқ‘— вҲҲрқ‘Ғ (рқ‘–)

We wonвҖҷt prove the general theorem here. The proof in Moser and Tardos (2010) is
beautifully written and not too long. I highly recommend it reading it. In the next
subsection, we will prove the correctness of the algorithm in a special case using a
neat idea known as entropy compression.
Remark 6.6.4 (Las Vegas versus Monte Carlo). Here are some important classes of

randomized algorithms:

98

6.6 Algorithmic local lemma
вҖў Monte Carlo algorithm (MC): a randomized algorithm that terminates with an
output, but there is a small probability that the output is incorrect;
вҖў Las Vegas algorithm (LV): a randomized algorithm that always returns a correct
answer, but may run for a long time (or possibly forever).
The MoserвҖ“Tardos algorithm is a LV algorithm whose expected runtime is bounded by
ГҚ
рқ‘– рқ‘Ҙрқ‘– /(1 вҲ’ рқ‘Ҙрқ‘– ), which is usually at most polynomial in the parameters of the problem.
We are usually interested in randomized algorithms whose running time is small (e.g.,
at most a polynomial of the input size).
We can convert an efficient LV algorithm into an efficient MC algorithm as follows:
suppose the LV algorithm has expected running time рқ‘Ү, and now we run the algorithm
but if it takes more than рқҗ¶рқ‘Ү time, then halt and declare a failure. MarkovвҖҷs inequality
then shows that the algorithm fails with probability вүӨ 1/рқҗ¶.
However, it is not always possible to convert an efficient MC algorithm into an efficient
LV algorithm. Starting with an MC algorithm, one might hope to repeatedly run it
until a correct answer has been found. However, there might not be an efficient way to
check the answer.
For example, consider the problem of finding a Ramsey coloring, specifically, 2edge-coloring of рқҗҫрқ‘ӣ without a monochromatic clique of size вүҘ 100 log2 рқ‘ӣ. A uniform
random coloring works with overwhelming probability, as can be checked by a simple
union bound (see Theorem 1.1.2). However, we do not have an efficient way to check
whether the random edge-coloring indeed has the desired property. It is a major open
problem to find an LV algorithm for finding such an edge-coloring.

Entropy compression argument
We now give a simple and elegant proof for a special case of the above algorithm, due
to Moser (2009). Actually, the argument in his paper is quite a bit more complicated.
Moser presented a version of the proof below in a conference, and his ideas were
popularized by Fortnow and Tao. (Fortnow called MoserвҖҷs talk вҖңone of the best STOC
talks everвҖқ). Tao introduced the phase entropy compression argument to describe
MoserвҖҷs influential idea. (We wonвҖҷt use the language of entropy here, and instead use a
more elementary argument involving counting and the pigeonhole principle. We will
discuss entropy in Chapter 10.)
To keep the argument simple, we work in the setting of рқ‘ҳ-CNFs. Recall from Example 6.1.6 that a рқ’Ң-CNF formula (conjunctive normal form) consist of a logical
conjunction (i.e., and, вҲ§) of clauses, where each clause is a disjunction (i.e., or, вҲЁ)
of exactly рқ‘ҳ literals. We shall require that the рқ‘ҳ literals of each clause use distinct

99

6 LovГЎsz Local Lemma
variables (рқ‘Ҙ 1 , . . . , рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘Ғ ), and each variable appears either in its positive рқ‘Ҙрқ‘– or negative
form рқ‘Ҙрқ‘– . For example, here is a 3-CNF with 4 clauses on 6 variables:
(рқ‘Ҙ 1 вҲЁ рқ‘Ҙ 2 вҲЁ рқ‘Ҙ 3 ) вҲ§ (рқ‘Ҙ 1 вҲЁ рқ‘Ҙ2 вҲЁ рқ‘Ҙ 4 ) вҲ§ (рқ‘Ҙ 2 вҲЁ рқ‘Ҙ4 вҲЁ рқ‘Ҙ 5 ) вҲ§ (рқ‘Ҙ 3 вҲЁ рқ‘Ҙ5 вҲЁ рқ‘Ҙ 6 ).
The problem is to find a satisfying assignment with boolean variables so that the
expression output to TRUE.
Algorithm 6.6.5 (Moser вҖңfix-itвҖқ)

input : a рқ‘ҳ-CNF
output : a satisfying assignment
Initialize by setting all variables to arbitrary values;
2 while there is some violated clause рқҗ¶ do
3
fix (рқҗ¶);
1

Subroutine fix (clause рқҗ¶) :
5
Resample the variables in рқҗ¶ uniformly at random;
6
while there is some violated clause рқҗ· that shares a variable with рқҗ¶ do
7
fix (рқҗ·);

4

(We can make the algorithm more well defined by specifying a way to pick an вҖңarbitraryвҖқ choice, e.g.,
the lexicographically first choice. Also, in Line 6, we allow taking рқҗ· = рқҗ¶.)

Theorem 6.6.6 (Correctness of MoserвҖҷs algorithm)

Given a рқ‘ҳ-CNF where every clause shares variables with at most 2 рқ‘ҳвҲ’3 other clauses,
Algorithm 6.6.5 output a satisfying assignment with expected running time at most
polynomial in the number of variables and clauses.
Note that the LovГЎsz local lemma guarantees the existence of a solution if each clause
shares variables with at most 2 рқ‘ҳ /рқ‘’ вҲ’ 1 clauses (each clause is violated with probability
exactly 2вҲ’рқ‘ҳ in a uniform random assignment of variables). So the theorem above is
tight up to an unimportant constant factor.
Lemma 6.6.7 (Outer while loop)

Each clause of the рқ‘ҳ-CNF appears at most once as a violated clause in the outer while
loop (Line 2).
Proof. Given an assignment of variables, by calling fix(рқҗ¶) for any clause рқҗ¶, any

clause that was previously satisfied remains satisfied after the completion of the execution of fix(рқҗ¶). Furthermore, рқҗ¶ becomes satisfied after the function call. Thus, once
fix(рқҗ¶) is called, рқҗ¶ can never show up again as a violated clause in Line 2.
в–Ў

100

6.6 Algorithmic local lemma

Lemma 6.6.8 (The number of recursive calls to fix)

Fix a рқ‘ҳ-CNF on рқ‘ӣ variables where every clause shares variables with at most 2 рқ‘ҳвҲ’3
other clauses. Also fix a clause рқҗ¶0 and some assignment of variables. Then, in an
execution of fix(рқҗ¶0 ), for any positive integer в„“,
P(there are at least в„“ recursive calls to fix in Line 7) вүӨ 2вҲ’в„“+рқ‘ӣ+1 .
It follows that the expected number of recursive calls to fix is рқ‘ӣ + рқ‘Ӯ (1). Thus, in
the Moser algorithm (Algorithm 6.6.5), the expected total number of calls to fix is
рқ‘ҡрқ‘ӣ + рқ‘Ӯ (рқ‘ҡ), where рқ‘ӣ is the number of variables and рқ‘ҡ is the number of clauses. This
proves the correctness of the algorithm (Theorem 6.6.6).
Proof. Let us formalize the randomness in the algorithm by first initializing a random

string of bits. Specifically, let рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ {0, 1} рқ‘ҳв„“ be generated uniformly at random. Whenever the a clause in resampled in Line 5, one replaces the variables in the clause by
the next рқ‘ҳ bits from рқ‘Ҙ. Furthermore, if the line Line 7 is called for the в„“-th time, we
halt the algorithm and declare a failure (as we would have run out of random bits to
resample had we continued).
At the same time, we keep an execution trace which keeps track of which clauses got
called fix, and also when the inner while loop Line 6 ends. Note that the very first
call to fix(рқҗ¶0 ) is not included in the execution trace since it is already given as fixed
and so we donвҖҷt need to include this information. Here is an example of an execution
trace, writing C7 for the 7th clause in the рқ‘ҳ-CNF:
fix(C7) called
fix(C4) called
fix(C7) called
while loop ended
fix(C2) called
while loop ended
while loop ended
...
For illustration, here is the example of how clause variables could intersect:
C2: ****
C4:
****
C7:
****
It is straightforward to deduce which while loop ended corresponds to which fix
call by reading the execution trace and keeping track of a first-in-first-out stack.

101

6 LovГЎsz Local Lemma
Encoding the execution trace as a bit string. We fix at the beginning some canonical
order of all clauses (e.g., lexicographic). It would be too expensive to refer to each
clause in its absolute position in this order (this is an important point!). Instead, we
note that every clause shares variables with at most 2 рқ‘ҳвҲ’3 other clauses, and only these
вүӨ 2 рқ‘ҳвҲ’3 could be called in the inner while loop in Line 6. So we can record which one
got called using a рқ‘ҳ вҲ’ 3 bit string.
вҖў fix(рқҗ·) called: suppose this was called inside an execution of fix(рқҗ¶), and
рқҗ· is the рқ‘—-th clause among all clauses sharing a variable with рқҗ¶, then record in
the execution trace bit string 0 followed by exactly в„“ вҲ’ 3 bits giving the binary
representation of рқ‘— (prepended by zeros to get exactly в„“ вҲ’ 3 bits).
вҖў while loop ended: record 1 in the execution trace bit string.
Note that one can recover the execution trace from the above bit string encoding.
Now, suppose the algorithm terminates as a failure due to fix being called the в„“-th
time. Here is the key claim.
Key claim (recovering randomness). At the moment right before the в„“-th recursive call to fix on Line 7, we can completely recover рқ‘Ҙ from the current variable
assignments and the execution trace.
Note that all в„“рқ‘ҳ random bits in рқ‘Ҙ have been used up at this point.
To see the key claim, note that from the execution trace, we can determine which clauses
were resampled and in what order. Furthermore, if fix(рқҗ·) was called on Line 7, then
рқҗ· must have been violated right before the call, and there is a unique possibility for
the violating assignment to рқҗ· right before the call (e.g., if рқҗ· = рқ‘Ҙ 1 вҲЁ рқ‘Ҙ2 вҲЁ рқ‘Ҙ 3 , then the
only violating assignment is (рқ‘Ҙ 1 , рқ‘Ҙ2 , рқ‘Ҙ3 ) = (0, 0, 1)). We can then rewind history, and
put the reassigned values to рқҗ· back into the random bit string рқ‘Ҙ to complete recover рқ‘Ҙ.
How long can the execution bit string be? It has length вүӨ в„“(рқ‘ҳ вҲ’ 1). Indeed, each of the
вүӨ в„“ recursive calls to fix produces рқ‘ҳ вҲ’ 2 bits for the call to fix and 1 bit for ending
the while loop. So the total number of possible execution strings is вүӨ 2в„“(рқ‘ҳвҲ’1)+1 (the
+1 accounts for variable lengths, though it can removed with a more careful analysis).
Thus, the key claim implies that each рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ {0, 1}в„“рқ‘ҳ that leads to a failed execution
produces a unique pair (variable assignment, execution bit string). Thus
P(вүҘ в„“ recursive calls to fix) 2в„“рқ‘ҳ = |{рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ {0, 1}рқ‘ӣ leading to failure}| вүӨ 2рқ‘ӣ 2в„“(рқ‘ҳвҲ’1)+1 .
Therefore, the failure probability is вүӨ 2вҲ’в„“+рқ‘ӣ+1 .

в–Ў

Remark 6.6.9 (Entropy compression). Tao use the phrase вҖңentropy compressionвҖқ to

describe this argument. The intuition is that the recoverability of the random bit string

102

6.6 Algorithmic local lemma
рқ‘Ҙ means that we are somehow вҖңcompressingвҖқ a в„“рқ‘ҳ-bit random string into a shorter
length losslessly, but that would be impossible. Each call to fix uses up рқ‘ҳ random bits
and converts it to рқ‘ҳ вҲ’ 1 bits to the execute trace (plus at most рқ‘ӣ bits of extra information,
namely the current variables assignment, and this is viewed as a constant amount of
information), and this conversion is reversible. So we are вҖңcompressing entropy.вҖқ The
conservation of information tells us that we cannot losslessly compress рқ‘ҳ random bits
to рқ‘ҳ вҲ’ 1 bits for very long.
Remark 6.6.10 (Relationship between the two proofs of the local lemma?). The

above proof, along with extensions of these ideas in Moser and Tardos (2010), seems
to give a completely different proof of the local lemma than the one we saw at the
beginning of the chapter. Is there some way to relate these seemingly completely
different proofs? Are they secretly the same proof? We do not know. This is an
interesting open-ended research problem.

7 Correlation Inequalities
7.1 HarrisвҖ“FKG inequality
Recall that рқҗҙ вҠҶ {0, 1}рқ‘ӣ is called an increasing event (also: increasing property, upset) if рқҗҙ is upwards-closed, meaning that whenever рқ‘Ҙ is in рқҗҙ, then everything above рқ‘Ҙ
in the boolean lattice also lies in рқҗҙ. In other words,
if рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ рқҗҙ and рқ‘Ҙ вүӨ рқ‘Ұ (coordinatewise), then рқ‘Ұ вҲҲ рқҗҙ.
Similarly, a decreasing event is defined by a downward closed collection of subset of
{0, 1}рқ‘ӣ . A subset рқҗҙ вҠҶ {0, 1}рқ‘ӣ is increasing if and only if its complement рқҗҙ вҠҶ {0, 1}рқ‘ӣ
is decreasing.
The main theorem of this chapter tells us that
increasing events of independent variables are positively correlated .
Theorem 7.1.1 (Harris 1960)

If рқҗҙ and рқҗө are increasing events of independent boolean random variables, then
P( рқҗҙрқҗө) вүҘ P( рқҗҙ)P(рқҗө).
Equivalently, we can write P ( рқҗҙ | рқҗө) вүҘ P( рқҗҙ).
Remark 7.1.2 (Independence assumption). It is important that the boolean random

variables are independent, also they do not have to be identically distributed.
There are other important settings where the independence assumption can be relaxed.
This is important for certain statistical physics models, where much of this theory
originally arose. Indeed, the above inequality is often called the FKG inequality,
attributed to Fortuin, Kasteleyn, Ginibre (1971), who proved a more general result in
the setting of distributive lattices, which we will not discuss here (see AlonвҖ“Spencer).
Remark 7.1.3 (Percolation). Many of such inequalities were initially introduced for

the study of percolations. A classic setting of this problem takes place in infinite
grid with vertices Z2 with edges connecting adjacent vertices at distance 1. Suppose

107

7 Correlation Inequalities
we keep each edge of this infinite grid with probability рқ‘қ independently, what is the
probability that the origin is part of an infinite component (in which case we say
that there is вҖңpercolationвҖқ)? This is supposed to an idealized mathematical model
of how a fluid permeates through a medium. Harris showed that with probability 1,
percolation does not occur for рқ‘қ вүӨ 1/2. A later breakthrough of Kesten (1980) shows
that percolation occurs with probability 1 for all рқ‘қ > 1/2. Thus the вҖңbond percolation
thresholdвҖқ for Z2 is exactly 1/2. Such exact results are extremely rare.
Example 7.1.4. Here is a quick application of HarrisвҖҷ inequality to a random graph

рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, рқ‘қ):
P(planar | connected) вүӨ P(planar).
Indeed, being planar is a decreasing property, whereas being connected is an increasing
property.
We state and prove a more general result, which says that independent random variables
possess positive association.
Let each О©рқ‘– be a linearly ordered set (i.e., {0, 1}, R) and рқ‘Ҙрқ‘– вҲҲ О©рқ‘– with respect to some
probability distribution independent for each рқ‘–. We say that a function рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ 1 , . . . , рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘ӣ )
is monotone increasing if
рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ) вүӨ рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ұ) whenever рқ‘Ҙ вүӨ рқ‘Ұ coordinatewise.

Theorem 7.1.5 (Harris)

If рқ‘“ and рқ‘” are monotone increasing functions of independent random variables, then
E[ рқ‘“ рқ‘”] вүҘ (E рқ‘“ )(Eрқ‘”).
This version of Harris inequality implies the earlier version by setting рқ‘“ = 1 рқҗҙ and
рқ‘” = 1рқҗө .

Corollary 7.1.6 (Decreasing events and multiple events)

Let рқҗҙ and рқҗө be events on independent random variables.
(a) If рқҗҙ and рқҗө are decreasing, then P( рқҗҙ вҲ§ рқҗө) вүҘ P( рқҗҙ)P(рқҗө).
(b) If рқҗҙ is increasing and рқҗө is decreasing, then P( рқҗҙ вҲ§ рқҗө) вүӨ P( рқҗҙ)P(рқҗө).
If рқҗҙ1 , . . . , рқҗҙ рқ‘ҳ are all increasing (or all decreasing) events on independent random
variables, then
P( рқҗҙ1 В· В· В· рқҗҙ рқ‘ҳ ) вүҘ P( рқҗҙ1 ) В· В· В· P( рқҗҙ рқ‘ҳ ).
Proof. For the second inequality, note that the complement рқҗө is increasing, so
Harris

P( рқҗҙрқҗө) = P( рқҗҙ) вҲ’ P( рқҗҙрқҗө) вүӨ P( рқҗҙ) вҲ’ P( рқҗҙ)P(рқҗө) = P( рқҗҙ)P(рқҗө).
The proof of the first inequality is similar. For the last inequality we apply the Harris
inequality repeatedly.

7.2 Applications to random graphs

Maximum degree
Question 7.2.4

WhatвҖҷs the probability that the maximum degree of рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, 1/2) is at most рқ‘ӣ/2?
For each vertex рқ‘Ј, deg(рқ‘Ј) вүӨ рқ‘ӣ/2 is a decreasing event with probability just slightly
over 1/2. So by Harris inequality, the probability that every рқ‘Ј has deg(рқ‘Ј) вүӨ рқ‘ӣ/2 is at
least вүҘ 2вҲ’рқ‘ӣ .
It turns out that the appearance of high degree vertices is much more correlated than
the independent case. The truth is exponentially more than the above bound.
Theorem 7.2.5 (Riordan and Selby 2000)

P(maxdeg рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, 1/2) вүӨ рқ‘ӣ/2) = (0.6102 В· В· В· + рқ‘ң(1)) рқ‘ӣ
Instead of giving a proof, we consider an easier continuous model of the problem that
motivates the numerical answer. Building on this intuition, Riordan and Selby (2000)
proved the result in the random graph setting, although this is beyond the scope of this
class.
In a random graphs, we assign independent Bernoulli random variables on edges of a
complete graph. Instead, let us assign independent standard normal random variables
to each edge of the complete graph.
Proposition 7.2.6 (Max degree with normal random edge labels)

Assign an independent standard normal random variable рқ‘Қрқ‘ўрқ‘Ј to each edge of рқҗҫрқ‘ӣ . Let
ГҚ
рқ‘Ҡрқ‘Ј = рқ‘ўвү рқ‘Ј рқ‘Қрқ‘ўрқ‘Ј be the sum of the labels of the edges incident to a vertex рқ‘Ј. Then
P(рқ‘Ҡрқ‘Ј вүӨ 0 вҲҖрқ‘Ј) = (0.6102 В· В· В· + рқ‘ң(1)) рқ‘ӣ
The event рқ‘Ҡрқ‘Ј вүӨ 0 is supposed to model the event that the degree at vertex рқ‘Ј is less
than рқ‘ӣ/2. Of course, other than intuition, there is no justification here that these two
models should behave similarly
We have P(рқ‘Ҡрқ‘Ј вүӨ 0) = 1/2. Since each {рқ‘Ҡрқ‘Ј вүӨ 0} is a decreasing event of the
independent edge labels, HarrisвҖҷ inequality tells us that
P(рқ‘Ҡрқ‘Ј вүӨ 0 вҲҖрқ‘Ј) вүҘ 2вҲ’рқ‘ӣ .
The truth turns out to be significantly greater.
Proof sketch of Proposition 7.2.6. The tuple (рқ‘Ҡрқ‘Ј )рқ‘ЈвҲҲ[рқ‘ӣ] has a joint normal distribution,

with each coordinate variance рқ‘ӣ вҲ’ 1 and pairwise covariance 1. So (рқ‘Ҡрқ‘Ј )рқ‘ЈвҲҲ[рқ‘ӣ] has the

7.2 Applications to random graphs

variables. Prove that there are two disjoint subsets рқ‘Ҷ and рқ‘Ү of these random
variables so that рқҗҙ depends only on рқ‘Ҷ and рқҗө depends only on рқ‘Ү.

113

8 Janson Inequalities
We present a collection of inequalities, known collectively as Janson inequalities
(Janson 1990). These tools allow us to estimate lower tail large deviation probabilities.
A typical application of JansonвҖҷs inequality allows us to upper bound the probability
that a random graph рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, рқ‘қ) does not contain any copy of some subgraph. Compared
to the second moment method from Chapter 4, Janson inequalities (which is applicable
in more limited setups) gives much better bounds, usually with exponential decays.

8.1 Probability of non-existence
The following setup should be a reminiscent of both the second moment method as
well as LovГЎsz local lemma (the random variable model).

в–Ў

Remark 8.1.4 (History). JansonвҖҷs original proof was via analytic interpolation. The

above proof is based on Boppana and Spencer (1989) with a modification by Warnke
(personal communication). It has some similarities to the proof of LovГЎsz local lemma
from Section 6.1. The above proof incorporates ideas from Riordan and Warnke
(2015), who extended JansonвҖҷs inequality from principal up-set to general up-sets.
Indeed, the above proof only requires that the events рқҗҙрқ‘– are increasing, whereas earlier
proofs of the result (e.g., the proof in AlonвҖ“Spencer) requires the full assumption of
Setup 8.1.1, namely that each рқҗҙрқ‘– is an event of the form рқ‘Ҷрқ‘– вҠҶ рқ‘…рқ‘– (i.e., a principal
up-set).

In fact, the number of triangles in рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, рқ‘җ/рқ‘ӣ) converges to a Poisson distribution
with mean рқ‘җ3 /6. On the other hand, when рқ‘қ вү« 1/рқ‘ӣ, the number of triangles is
asymptotically normal.
What about if рқ‘қ вү« рқ‘ӣвҲ’1/2 , so that О” вү« рқңҮ. Janson inequality I does not tell us anything
nontrivial. Do we still expect the triangle-free probability to be рқ‘’ вҲ’(1+рқ‘ң(1))рқңҮ , or even
вүӨ рқ‘’ вҲ’рқ‘җрқңҮ ?

Remark 8.1.9. If рқңҮ вҶ’ вҲһ and О” вүӘ рқңҮ2 , then Janson inequality II implies P(рқ‘Ӣ = 0) =

Remark 8.1.11. Sharper results are known. Here are some highlights.
2

1. The number of triangle-free graphs on рқ‘ӣ vertices is 2 (1+рқ‘ң(1))рқ‘ӣ /4 . In fact, an even
stronger statement is true: almost all (i.e., 1вҲ’рқ‘ң(1) fraction) рқ‘ӣ-vertex triangle-free
graphs are bipartite (ErdЕ‘s, Kleitman, and Rothschild 1976).
вҲҡпёҒ
вҲҡ
2. If рқ‘ҡ вүҘ рқҗ¶рқ‘ӣ3/2 log рқ‘ӣ for any constant рқҗ¶ > 3/4 (and this is best possible), then
almost all all рқ‘ӣ-vertex рқ‘ҡ-edge triangle-free graphs are bipartite (Osthus, PrГ¶mel,
and Taraz 2003). This result has been extended to рқҗҫрқ‘ҹ -free graphs for every fixed
рқ‘ҹ (Balogh, Morris, SamotДі, and Warnke 2016).
3. For рқ‘ӣвҲ’1/2 вүӘ рқ‘қ вүӘ 1, (ЕҒuczak 2000)
вҲ’ log P(рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, рқ‘қ) is triangle-free) вҲј вҲ’ log P(рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, рқ‘қ) is bipartite) вҲј рқ‘ӣ2 рқ‘қ/4.
This result was generalized to general рқҗ»-free graphs using the powerful recent
method of hypergraph containers (Balogh, Morris, and SamotДі 2015).

Remark 8.2.6. The leading constants were determined by Lubetzky and Zhao (2017)

frameworks that gave the above theorem for sufficiently slowly decaying рқ‘қ вүҘ рқ‘ӣвҲ’рқ‘җ .
For the corresponding problem for lower tails, see Kozma and SamotДі (2023) for an

The exact leading constant is known only for sufficiently small рқӣҝ > 0, where the answer

decrement in edge densities for the random graph. In contrast, for рқӣҝ close to 1, we
expect (though cannot prove) that the typical structure of a conditioned random graph
is close to a two-block model (Zhao 2017).

The list-chromatic number (also called choosability) of a graph рқҗә is defined to the minimum рқ‘ҳ
such that if every vertex of рқҗә is assigned a list of рқ‘ҳ acceptable colors, then there exists a proper
coloring of рқҗә where every vertex is colored by one of its acceptable colors.

9 Concentration of Measure
9.1 Bounded differences inequality
Recall that the Chernoff bound allows to prove exponential tail bounds for sums of
independent random variables. For example, if рқ‘Қ is a sum of рқ‘ӣ independent Bernoulli
random variables, then
2
P(|рқ‘Қ вҲ’ Eрқ‘Қ | вүҘ рқ‘Ў) вүӨ 2рқ‘’ вҲ’2рқ‘Ў /рқ‘ӣ .
In this chapter, we develop tools for proving similar tail bounds for other random
variables that do not necessarily arise as a sum of independent random variables.
The next theorem says:
A Lipschitz function of many independent random variables is concentrated.
We will prove the following important and useful result, known by several names:
McDiarmidвҖҷs inequality, AzumaвҖ“Hoeffding inequality, and bounded differences
inequality.
Theorem 9.1.1 (Bounded differences inequality)

Let рқ‘Ӣ1 вҲҲ О©1 , . . . , рқ‘Ӣрқ‘ӣ вҲҲ О©рқ‘ӣ be independent random variables. Suppose рқ‘“ : О©1 Г— В· В· В· Г—
О©рқ‘ӣ вҶ’ R satisfies
рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ 1 , . . . , рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘ӣ ) вҲ’ рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ 1вҖІ , . . . , рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘ӣвҖІ ) вүӨ 1
(9.1)

9.2 Martingales concentration inequalities
Definition 9.2.1

A martingale is a random real sequence рқ‘Қ0 , рқ‘Қ1 , . . . such that for every рқ‘Қрқ‘ӣ , E|рқ‘Қрқ‘ӣ | < вҲһ
and
E[рқ‘Қрқ‘ӣ+1 |рқ‘Қ0 , . . . , рқ‘Қрқ‘ӣ ] = рқ‘Қрқ‘ӣ .
(To be more formal, we should talk about filtrations of a probability space . . . )
Example 9.2.2 (Random walks with independent steps). If (рқ‘Ӣрқ‘– )рқ‘–вүҘ0 is a sequence of

130

9.2 Martingales concentration inequalities
independent random variables with Eрқ‘Ӣрқ‘– = 0 for all рқ‘–, then the partial sums рқ‘Қрқ‘ӣ =
is a Martingale.

ГҚ

рқ‘–вүӨрқ‘ӣ рқ‘Ӣрқ‘–

Example 9.2.3 (Betting strategy). Betting on a sequence of fair coin tosses. After

round, you are allow to change your bet. Let рқ‘Қрқ‘ӣ be your balance after the рқ‘ӣ-th round.
Then рқ‘Қрқ‘ӣ is always a martingale regardless of your strategy.
Originally, the term вҖңmartingaleвҖқ referred to the betting strategy where one doubles
the bet each time until the first win and then stop betting. Then, with probability 1,
рқ‘Қрқ‘ӣ = 1 for all sufficiently large рқ‘ӣ. (Why does this вҖңfree moneyвҖқ strategy not actually
work?)
The next example is especially important to us.
Example 9.2.4 (Doob martingale). Let рқ‘Ӣ1 , . . . , рқ‘Ӣрқ‘ӣ be a random sequence (not nec-

essarily independent, though they often are independent in practice). Consider a
function рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ӣ1 , . . . , рқ‘Ӣрқ‘ӣ ). Let рқ‘Қрқ‘– be the expected value of рқ‘“ after вҖңrevealingвҖқ (exposing)
рқ‘Ӣ1 , . . . , рқ‘Ӣрқ‘– , i.e.,
рқ‘Қрқ‘– = E[ рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ӣ1 , . . . , рқ‘Ӣрқ‘ӣ )|рқ‘Ӣ1 , . . . , рқ‘Ӣрқ‘– ].
So рқ‘Қрқ‘– is the expected value of the random variable рқ‘Қ = рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ӣ1 , . . . , рқ‘Ӣрқ‘ӣ ) after seeing the
first рқ‘– arguments, and letting the remaining arguments be random. Then рқ‘Қ0 , . . . , рқ‘Қрқ‘ӣ is
a martingale (why?). It satisfies рқ‘Қ0 = Eрқ‘Қ (a non-random quantity) and рқ‘Қрқ‘ӣ = рқ‘Қ (the
random variable that we care about), and thereby offering a way to interpolate between
the two.
Example 9.2.5 (Edge-exposure martingale). We can reveal the random graph рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, рқ‘қ)

by first fixing an order on all unordered pairs of [рқ‘ӣ] and then revealing in order whether
each pair is an edge. For any graph parameter рқ‘“ (рқҗә) we can produce a martingale
рқ‘Ӣ0 , рқ‘Ӣ1 , . . . , рқ‘Ӣ ( рқ‘ӣ) where рқ‘Қрқ‘– is the conditional expectation of рқ‘“ (рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, рқ‘қ)) after revealing
2
whether there are edges for first рқ‘– pairs of vertices. See Figure 9.1 for an example.
Example 9.2.6 (Vertex-exposure martingale). Similar to the previous example, ex-

cept that we now first fix an order on the vertex set, and, at the рқ‘–-th step, with 0 вүӨ рқ‘– вүӨ рқ‘ӣ,
we reveal all edges whose endpoints are contained in the first рқ‘– vertices. See Figure 9.1
for an example.
Sometimes it is better to use the edge-exposure martingale and sometimes it is better to
use the vertex-exposure martingale. It depends on the application. There is a trade-off
between the length of the martingale and the control on the bounded differences.
The main result is that a martingale with bounded differences must be concentrated. The following fundamental result is called AzumaвҖҷs inequality or the AzumaвҖ“
Hoeffding inequality.

Remark 9.2.13. AzumaвҖҷs inequality (Theorem 9.2.9) is more versatile than (Theo-

potentially be smaller than in Theorem 9.1.3. This will be useful in some applications,
including one that we will see later in the chapter.

9.3 Chromatic number of random graphs
Concentration of the chromatic number
Even before BollobГЎs (1988) showed that рқң’(рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, 1/2)) вҲј 2 logрқ‘ӣ рқ‘ӣ whp (Theorem 8.3.2),
2
using the bounded difference inequality, it was already known that the chromatic
вҲҡ
number of a random graph must be concentrated in a рқ‘Ӯ ( рқ‘ӣ) window around its mean.
The following application shows that one can prove concentration around the mean
without even knowing where is the mean!
Theorem 9.3.1 (Shamir and Spencer 1987)

For every рқңҶ вүҘ 0, the chromatic number of a random graph рқ‘Қ = рқң’(рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, рқ‘қ)) satisfies
вҲҡ
2
P(|рқ‘Қ вҲ’ Eрқ‘Қ | вүҘ рқңҶ рқ‘ӣ вҲ’ 1) вүӨ 2рқ‘’ вҲ’2рқңҶ .
Proof. Let рқ‘ү = [рқ‘ӣ], and consider each vertex labeled graph as an element of О©2 Г—

В· В· В· Г— О©рқ‘ӣ where О©рқ‘– = {0, 1}рқ‘–вҲ’1 and its coordinates correspond to edges whose larger
coordinate is рқ‘– (cf. the vertex-exposure martingale Example 9.2.6). If two graphs рқҗә
and рқҗә вҖІ differ only in edges incident to one vertex рқ‘Ј, then | рқң’(рқҗә) вҲ’ рқң’(рқҗә вҖІ)| вүӨ 1 since,
given a proper coloring of рқҗә using рқң’(рқҗә) colors, one can obtain a proper coloring
of рқҗә вҖІ using рқң’(рқҗә) + 1 colors by using a new color for рқ‘Ј. Theorem 9.1.3 implies the
result.
в–Ў
Remark 9.3.2 (Non-concentration of the chromatic number). Heckel (2021) showed

that the рқң’(рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, 1/2)) is not concentrated on any interval of length рқ‘ӣрқ‘җ for any constant
рқ‘җ < 1/4. This was the opposite of what most experts believed in. It has been
conjectured that width of the window of concentrations fluctuates between рқ‘ӣ1/4+рқ‘ң(1) to
рқ‘ӣ1/2+рқ‘ң(1) depending on рқ‘ӣ.

135

9 Concentration of Measure

Clique number, again
Previously in Section 8.3, we used Janson inequalities to prove the following exponentially small bound on the probability that рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, 1/2) has small clique number. This was a crucial step in the proof of BollobГЎsвҖҷ theorem (Theorem 8.3.2) that
рқң’(рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, 1/2)) вҲј рқ‘ӣ/(2 log2 рқ‘ӣ) whp. Here we give a different proof using the bounded
difference inequality instead of Janson inequalities. The proof below in fact was the
original approach of BollobГЎs (1988).
Lemma 9.3.3 (Same as Lemma 8.3.3)

9.4 Isoperimetric inequalities: a geometric
perspective
We shall explore the following connection, which are two sides of the same coin:

Geometry
Isoperimetric inequalities

139

9 Concentration of Measure
Milman recognized the importance of the concentration of measure phenomenon,
which he heavily promoted in the 1970вҖҷs. The subject was have been since then
extensively developed. It plays a central role in probability theory, the analysis of
Banach spaces, and it also has been influential in theoretical computer science.

Euclidean space
The classic isoperimetric theorem in Rрқ‘ӣ says that that among all subset of Rрқ‘ӣ of given
volume, the ball has the smallest surface volume. (The word вҖңisoperimetricвҖқ refers to
fixing the perimeter; equivalently we fix the surface area and ask to maximize volume.)
This result (at least in two-dimensions) was known to the Greeks, but rigorous proofs
were only found in towards the end of the nineteenth century.
Let (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘‘ рқ‘Ӣ ) be a metric space. Let рқҗҙ вҠҶ рқ‘Ӣ. For any рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ рқ‘Ӣ, write рқ‘‘ рқ‘Ӣ (рқ‘Ҙ, рқҗҙ) :=
inf рқ‘ҺвҲҲрқҗҙ рқ‘‘ рқ‘Ӣ (рқ‘Ҙ, рқ‘Һ) for the distance from рқ‘Ҙ to рқҗҙ. Denote the set of all points within
distance рқ‘Ў from рқҗҙ by
рқҗҙрқ‘Ў := {рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ рқ‘Ӣ : рқ‘‘ рқ‘Ӣ (рқ‘Ҙ, рқҗҙ) вүӨ рқ‘Ў}
(9.1)
This is also known as the radius-рқ’• neighborhood of рқ‘Ё. One can visualize рқҗҙрқ‘Ў by
вҖңexpandingвҖқ рқҗҙ by distance рқ‘Ў.
Theorem 9.4.1 (Isoperimetric inequality in Euclidean space)

Let рқҗҙ вҠҶ Rрқ‘ӣ be a measurable set, and let рқҗө вҠҶ Rрқ‘ӣ be a ball vol( рқҗҙ) = vol(рқҗө). Then, for
all рқ‘Ў вүҘ 0,
vol рқҗҙрқ‘Ў вүҘ vol рқҗөрқ‘Ў .
Remark 9.4.2. A clean way to prove the above inequality is via the BrunnвҖ“Minkowski

theorem.
Classically, the isoperimetric inequality is stated as (here рқң• рқҗҙ is the boundary of рқҗҙ)
volрқ‘ӣвҲ’1 рқң• рқҗҙ вүҘ volрқ‘ӣвҲ’1 рқң•рқҗө.
These two formulations are equivalent. Indeed, assuming Theorem 9.4.1, we have
volрқ‘ӣвҲ’1 рқң• рқҗҙ =

рқ‘ЎвҶ’0
рқ‘‘рқ‘Ў рқ‘Ў=0
рқ‘Ў
vol рқҗөрқ‘Ў вҲ’ vol рқҗө

= volрқ‘ӣвҲ’1 рқң•рқҗө.

Conversely, we can obtain the neighborhood version from the boundary version by
integrating (noting that рқҗөрқ‘Ў is always a ball).

The cube
We have an analogous result in the {0, 1}рқ‘ӣ with respect to Hamming distance.In
Hamming cube, HarperвҖҷs theorem gives the exact result. Below, for рқҗҙ вҠҶ {0, 1}рқ‘ӣ , we
write рқҗҙрқ‘Ў as in (9.1) for рқ‘Ӣ = {0, 1}рқ‘ӣ and рқ‘‘ рқ‘Ӣ being the Hamming distance.
Theorem 9.4.3 (Isoperimetic inequality in the Hamming cube; Harper 1966)

Let рқҗҙ вҠҶ {0, 1}рқ‘ӣ . Let рқҗө вҠҶ {0, 1}рқ‘ӣ be a Hamming ball with | рқҗҙ| вүҘ |рқҗө|. Then for all
рқ‘Ў вүҘ 0,
| рқҗҙрқ‘Ў | вүҘ |рқҗөрқ‘Ў |.
Remark 9.4.4. The above statement is tight when рқҗҙ has the same size as a Hamming



ball, i.e., when | рқҗҙ| = рқ‘ӣ0 + рқ‘ӣ1 + В· В· В· + рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳ for some integer рқ‘ҳ. Actually, more is true.
For any value of | рқҗҙ| and рқ‘Ў, the size of рқҗҙрқ‘Ў is minimized by taking рқҗҙ to be an initial
segment of {0, 1}рқ‘ӣ according to the simplicial ordering: first sort by Hamming weight,
and for ties, sort by lexicographic order. For more on this topic, particularly extremal
set theory, see the book Combinatorics by BollobГЎs (1986).

Combined with the isoperimetic inequality on the cube, we obtain the following
surprising consequence. Suppose we start with just half of the cube, and then expand
it by a bit (recall that the diameter of the cube is рқ‘ӣ, and we will be expanding it by
рқ‘ң(рқ‘ӣ)), then resulting expansion occupies nearly all of the cube.
Theorem 9.4.5 (Rapid expansion from half to 1 вҲ’ рқңҖ )

Let рқ‘Ў > 0. For every рқҗҙ вҠҶ {0, 1}рқ‘ӣ with | рқҗҙ| вүҘ 2рқ‘ӣвҲ’1 , we have
2

| рқҗҙрқ‘Ў | > (1 вҲ’ рқ‘’ вҲ’2рқ‘Ў /рқ‘ӣ )2рқ‘ӣ .
Proof. Let рқҗө = {рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ {0, 1} рқ‘ӣ : weight(рқ‘Ҙ) < рқ‘ӣ/2}, so that |рқҗө| вүӨ 2рқ‘ӣвҲ’1 вүӨ | рқҗҙ|. Then by

HarperвҖҷs theorem (Theorem 9.4.3),
2

| рқҗҙрқ‘Ў | вүҘ |рқҗөрқ‘Ў | = |{рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ {0, 1}рқ‘ӣ : weight(рқ‘Ҙ) < рқ‘ӣ/2 + рқ‘Ў}| > (1 вҲ’ рқ‘’ вҲ’2рқ‘Ў /рқ‘ӣ )2рқ‘ӣ
by the Chernoff bound.

Isoperimetry versus concentration
The above two proofs illustrate the link between geometric isoperimetric inequalities
and probabilistic concentration inequalities. Let know now state a simple result that

142

9.4 Isoperimetric inequalities: a geometric perspective
formalizes this connection.
Definition 9.4.7 (Lipschitz functions)

Given two metric spaces (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘‘ рқ‘Ӣ ) and (рқ‘Ң , рқ‘‘рқ‘Ң ), we say that a function рқ‘“ : рқ‘Ӣ вҶ’ рқ‘Ң is
рқ‘Ә-Lipschitz if
рқ‘‘рқ‘Ң ( рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ), рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ вҖІ)) вүӨ рқҗ¶рқ‘‘ рқ‘Ӣ (рқ‘Ҙ, рқ‘Ҙ вҖІ)

for all рқ‘Ҙ, рқ‘Ҙ вҖІ вҲҲ рқ‘Ӣ.

So the bounded differences inequality applies to Lipschitz functions with respect to
the Hamming distance. In particular, it tells us that if рқ‘“ : {0, 1}рқ‘ӣ вҶ’ R is 1-Lipschitz
(with respect to the Hamming distance on {0, 1}рқ‘ӣ ), it must be concentrated around its
mean with respect to the uniform measure on {0, 1}рқ‘ӣ :
2

P(| рқ‘“ вҲ’ E рқ‘“ | вүҘ рқ‘ӣрқңҶ) вүӨ 2рқ‘’ вҲ’2рқ‘ӣрқңҶ .
So рқ‘“ is almost constant almost everywhere. This is a counterintuitive high dimensional
phenomenon.
Theorem 9.4.8 (Equivalence between notions of concentration of measure)

Let рқ‘Ў, рқңҖ вүҘ 0. In a probability space (О©, P) equipped with a metric. The following are
equivalent:
(a) (Expansion/approximate isoperimetry) If рқҗҙ вҠҶ О© with P( рқҗҙ) вүҘ 1/2, then
P( рқҗҙрқ‘Ў ) вүҘ 1 вҲ’ рқңҖ.
(b) (Concentration of Lipschitz functions) If рқ‘“ : О© вҶ’ R is 1-Lipschitz and рқ‘ҡ вҲҲ R
satisfies P( рқ‘“ вүӨ рқ‘ҡ) вүҘ 1/2, then
P( рқ‘“ > рқ‘ҡ + рқ‘Ў) вүӨ рқңҖ.
Remark 9.4.9 (Median). In (b), we often take рқ‘ҡ to be a median of рқ‘“ , which is defined

to be a value such that P( рқ‘“ вүҘ рқ‘ҡ) вүҘ 1/2 and P( рқ‘“ вүӨ рқ‘ҡ) вүҘ 1/2 (the median always exists
but is not necessarily unique). For distributions with good concentration properties,
the median and mean are usually close to each other. For example, we leave it as an
2
exercise to check that if there is some рқ‘ҡ such that P(| рқ‘“ вҲ’ рқ‘ҡ| вүҘ рқ‘Ў) вүӨ 2рқ‘’ вҲ’рқ‘Ў /2 for all
рқ‘Ў вүҘ 0, then the mean and the medians of рқ‘“ all lie within рқ‘Ӯ (1) of рқ‘ҡ.
Proof. (a) =вҮ’ (b): Let рқҗҙ = {рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ О© : рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ) вүӨ рқ‘ҡ}. So P( рқҗҙ) вүҘ 1/2. Since рқ‘“ is

1-Lipschitz, we have рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ) вүӨ рқ‘ҡ + рқ‘Ў for all рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ рқҗҙрқ‘Ў . Thus by (a)
P( рқ‘“ > рқ‘ҡ + рқ‘Ў) вүӨ P( рқҗҙрқ‘Ў ) вүӨ рқңҖ.

143

9 Concentration of Measure
(b) =вҮ’ (a): Let рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ) = dist(рқ‘Ҙ, рқҗҙ) and рқ‘ҡ = 0. Then P( рқ‘“ вүӨ 0) = P( рқҗҙ) вүҘ 1/2. Also рқ‘“
is 1-Lipschitz. So by (b),
P( рқҗҙрқ‘Ў ) = P( рқ‘“ > рқ‘ҡ + рқ‘Ў) вүӨ рқңҖ.

в–Ў

Informally, we say that a space (or rather, a sequence of spaces), has concentration
of measure if рқңҖ decays rapidly as a function of рқ‘Ў in the above theorem (the notion of
вҖңLГ©vy familyвҖқ makes this precise). Earlier we saw that the Hamming cube exhibits has
concentration of measure. Other notable spaces with concentration of measure include
the sphere, Gauss space, orthogonal and unitary groups, postively-curved manifolds,
and the symmetric group.

The sphere
We discuss analogs of the concentration of measure phenomenon in high dimensional
geometry. This is rich and beautiful subject. An excellent introductory to this topic is
the survey An Elementary Introduction to Modern Convex Geometry by Ball (1997).
Recall the isoperimetric inequality in Rрқ‘ӣ says:
If рқҗҙ вҠҶ Rрқ‘ӣ has the same measure as ball рқҗө, then vol( рқҗҙрқ‘Ў ) вүҘ vol(рқҗөрқ‘Ў ) for all
рқ‘Ў вүҘ 0.
Analogous exact isoperimetric inequalities are known in several other spaces. We
already saw it for the boolean cube (Theorem 9.4.3). The case of sphere and Gaussian
space are particularly noteworthy. The following theorem is due to LГ©vy (вҲј1919).
Theorem 9.4.10 (LГ©vyвҖҷs isoperimetric inequality on the sphere)

On a sphere in Rрқ‘ӣ , let рқҗҙ be a measurable subset and рқҗө a spherical cap with volрқ‘ӣвҲ’1 ( рқҗҙ) =
volрқ‘ӣвҲ’1 (рқҗө). Then for all рқ‘Ў вүҘ 0,
volрқ‘ӣвҲ’1 ( рқҗҙрқ‘Ў ) вүҘ volрқ‘ӣвҲ’1 (рқҗөрқ‘Ў ).
We have the following upper bound estimate on the size of spherical caps.

Informally: every Lipschitz function on a high dimensional sphere is almost constant
almost everywhere.
This is a rather counterintuitive high-dimensional phenomenon.

Gauss space
Another related setting is the Gauss space, which is Rрқ‘ӣ equipped with the the probability measure рқӣҫрқ‘ӣ induced by the Gaussian random vector whose coordinates are рқ‘ӣ iid
standard normals, i.e., the normal random vector in Rрқ‘ӣ with covariance matrix рқҗјрқ‘ӣ . Its
2
probability density function of рқӣҫрқ‘ӣ at рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ Rрқ‘ӣ is (2рқңӢ) вҲ’рқ‘ӣ рқ‘’ вҲ’|рқ‘Ҙ| /2 . The metric on Rрқ‘ӣ is the
usual Euclidean metric.
What would an isoperimetric inequality in Gauss space look like?
Although earlier examples of isoperimetric optimizers were all balls, for the Gauss
space, the answer is actually a half-spaces, i.e., points on one side of some hyperplane.
The Gaussian isoperimetric inequality, below, was first shown independently by Borell
(1975) and Sudakov and TsirelвҖҷson (1974).
Theorem 9.4.15 (Gaussian isoperimetric inequality)

If рқҗҙ, рқҗ» вҠҶ Rрқ‘ӣ , рқҗ» a half-space, and рқӣҫ( рқҗҙ) = рқӣҫ(рқҗ»), then рқӣҫ( рқҗҙрқ‘Ў ) вүҘ рқӣҫ(рқҗ»рқ‘Ў ) for all рқ‘Ў вүҘ 0,
where рқӣҫ is the Gauss measure.

146

9.4 Isoperimetric inequalities: a geometric perspective
2

If рқҗ» = {рқ‘Ҙ 1 вүӨ 0}, then рқҗ»рқ‘Ў = {рқ‘Ҙ 1 вүӨ рқ‘Ў}, which has Gaussian measure вүҘ 1 вҲ’ рқ‘’ вҲ’рқ‘Ў /2 . Thus:
Corollary 9.4.16 (Concentration of measure for Gaussian vectors)

If рқ‘“ : Rрқ‘ӣ вҶ’ R is 1-Lipschitz, and рқ‘Қ is a vector of i.i.d. standard normals, then рқ‘Ӣ = рқ‘“ (рқ‘Қ)
satisfies, for some рқ‘ҡ,
2
P(|рқ‘Ӣ вҲ’ рқ‘ҡ| вүҘ рқ‘Ў) вүӨ 2рқ‘’ вҲ’рқ‘Ў /2 .
Here is a rather handwavy explanation why the half-space is a reasonable answer.
Consider {вҲ’1, 1} рқ‘ҡрқ‘ӣ , where both рқ‘ҡ and рқ‘ӣ are large. Let us group the coordinates of
{вҲ’1, 1} рқ‘ҡрқ‘ӣ into block of length рқ‘ҡ. The sum of entries in each block (after normalizing
вҲҡ
by рқ‘ҡ) approximates normal random variable by the central limit theorem.
In the Hamming cube, HarperвҖҷs theorem tells us Hamming balls are isoperimetric
optimizers. Since a Hamming ball in {вҲ’1, 1} рқ‘ҡрқ‘ӣ is given by all points whose sum of
coordinates is below a certain threshold, we should look at the analogous subset in the
Gauss space, which would then consist of all points whose sum of coordinates is below
a certain threshold. The set of all points whose of coordinate sum is below a certain
threshold is half-space. Note also that the Gaussian measure is radially symmetric.
The sphere as approximately a sum of independent Gaussians. The Gauss space is
a nice space to work with because a standard normal vector simultaneously possesses
two useful properties (and it is essentially the only such random vector to have both
properties):
(a) Rotational invariance
(b) Independence of coordinates
The squared-length of a random Gaussian vector is рқ‘Қ12 + В· В· В· + рқ‘Қрқ‘ӣ2 with iid рқ‘Қ1 , . . . , рқ‘Қрқ‘ӣ вҲҲ
вҲҡ
(e.g., by a straightforward
рқ‘Ғ (0, 1). It has mean рқ‘ӣ and a рқ‘Ӯ ( рқ‘ӣ) window of concentration
вҲҡпёҒ
вҲҡ
вҲҡ
adaptation of the Chernoff bound proof). Since рқ‘ӣ + рқ‘Ӯ ( рқ‘ӣ) = рқ‘ӣ + рқ‘Ӯ (1), the length
вҲҡ
of Gaussian vector is concentrated in a рқ‘Ӯ (1) window around рқ‘ӣ (the concentration can
also be deduced from the above corollary for рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ) = |рқ‘Ҙ|). So most of the distribution
вҲҡ
in the Gauss space lies within a constant distance of a sphere of radius рқ‘ӣ. Due to
rotational invariance, we see that a Gaussian distribution approximates the uniform
вҲҡ
distribution on sphere of radius рқ‘ӣ in high dimensions. In other words:
вҲҡ
random Gaussian vector вүҲ рқ‘ӣ В· random unit vector.
Random Gaussian vectors often yield easier calculations due to coordinate independence, and so they often give an accessible way to analyze random unit vectors.

with both italicized objects being isoperimetric optimizers in their respective spaces.

what we mean by рқңҺ-subGaussian.

JohnsonвҖ“Lindenstrauss Lemma
Given a set of рқ‘Ғ points in high-dimensional Euclidean space, the next result tells us
that one can embed them in рқ‘Ӯ (рқңҖ вҲ’2 log рқ‘Ғ) dimensions without sacrificing pairwise
distances by more than 1 Вұ рқңҖ factor. This is known as dimension reduction. It is an
important tool in many areas, from functional analysis to algorithms.
Theorem 9.4.22 (Johnson and Lindenstrauss 1982)

There exists a constant рқҗ¶ > 0 so that the following holds. Let рқңҖ > 0. Let рқ‘Ӣ be a set of
рқ‘Ғ points in Rрқ‘ҡ . Then for any рқ‘‘ > рқҗ¶рқңҖ вҲ’2 log рқ‘Ғ, there exists рқ‘“ : рқ‘Ӣ вҶ’ Rрқ‘‘ so that
(1 вҲ’ рқңҖ) |рқ‘Ҙ вҲ’ рқ‘Ұ| вүӨ | рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ) вҲ’ рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ұ)| вүӨ (1 + рқңҖ) |рқ‘Ҙ вҲ’ рқ‘Ұ|

for all рқ‘Ҙ, рқ‘Ұ вҲҲ рқ‘Ӣ.

Remark 9.4.23. Here the requirement рқ‘‘ > рқҗ¶рқңҖ вҲ’2 log рқ‘Ғ on the dimension is optimal

up to a constant factor (Larsen and Nelson 2017).

subspace chosen uniformly at random. The theorem then follows from the following

9.5 TalagrandвҖҷs inequality
Talagrand (1995) developed a powerful concentration inequality. It is applicable to
many combinatorial optimization problems on independent random inputs. The most
general form of TalagrandвҖҷs inequality can be somewhat difficult to grasp. So we start
by discussing a special case with an easier geometric statement. Though, to obtain the
full power of TalagrandвҖҷs inequality with combinatorial consequences, we will need
the full statement to be given later.
We omit the proof of TalagrandвҖҷs inequality (see the AlonвҖ“Spencer textbook or TaoвҖҷs
blog post) and instead focus on explaining the theorem and its applications.

Remark 9.5.18. If рқҗҙ has mean zero entries, then a moments computation shows that

Certifiable functions and longest increasing subsequence
An increasing subsequence of a permutation рқңҺ = (рқңҺ1 , . . . , рқңҺрқ‘ӣ ) is defined to be some
(рқңҺрқ‘–1 , . . . , рқңҺрқ‘–в„“ ) for some рқ‘–1 < В· В· В· < рқ‘–в„“ .
Question 9.5.19

How well is the length рқ‘Ӣ of the longest increasing subsequence of uniform random
permutation concentrated?
While the entries of рқңҺ are not independent, we can generate a uniform random permutation by taking iid uniform рқ‘Ҙ 1 , . . . , рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘ӣ вҲј Unif [0, 1] and let рқңҺ record the ordering of
the рқ‘Ҙрқ‘– вҖҷs. This trick converts the problem into one about independent random variables.
вҲҡ
We leave it as an exercise to deduce that рқ‘Ӣ is Оҳ( рқ‘ӣ) whp.
Changing one of the рқ‘Ҙрқ‘– вҖҷs changes LIS by at most 1, so the bounded differences inequality
вҲҡ
tells us that рқ‘Ӣ is рқ‘Ӯ ( рқ‘ӣ)-subGaussian. Can we do better?
The assertion that a permutation has an increasing permutation of length рқ‘  can be
checked by verifying рқ‘  coordinates of the permutation. TalagrandвҖҷs inequality
tells
вҲҡ
us that in such situations the typical fluctuation should be on the order рқ‘Ӯ ( Mрқ‘Ӣ), or
рқ‘Ӯ (рқ‘ӣ1/4 ) in this case.
Definition 9.5.20

Let О© = О©1 Г— В· В· В· Г— О©рқ‘ӣ . Let рқҗҙ вҠҶ О©. We say that рқҗҙ is рқ’”-certifiable if for every рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ рқҗҙ,
there exists a set рқҗј (рқ‘Ҙ) вҠҶ [рқ‘ӣ] with |рқҗј | вүӨ рқ‘  such that for every рқ‘Ұ вҲҲ О© with рқ‘Ҙрқ‘– = рқ‘Ұрқ‘– for all
рқ‘– вҲҲ рқҗј (рқ‘Ҙ), one has рқ‘Ұ вҲҲ рқҗҙ.
For example, for a random permutation as earlier, having an increasing subsequence
of length вүҘ рқ‘  is рқ‘ -certifiable (namely by the indices of the length рқ‘  increasing subsequence).

9.6 Euclidean traveling salesman problem
Given points рқ‘Ҙ 1 , . . . , рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘ӣ вҲҲ [0, 1] 2 , let рқҗҝ (рқ‘Ҙ 1 , . . . , рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘ӣ ) = рқҗҝ ({рқ‘Ҙ 1 , . . . , рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘ӣ }) denote the
length of the shortest tour through all given points and returns to its starting point.
Equivalently, рқҗҝ (рқ‘Ҙ 1 , . . . , рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘ӣ ) is the minimum of
|рқ‘Ҙ рқңҺ(1) вҲ’ рқ‘Ҙ рқңҺ(2) | + |рқ‘Ҙ рқңҺ(2) вҲ’ рқ‘Ҙ рқңҺ(3) | + В· В· В· + |рқ‘Ҙ рқңҺ(рқ‘ӣ) вҲ’ рқ‘Ҙ рқңҺ(1) |
as рқңҺ ranges over all permutations of [рқ‘ӣ]. This Euclidean traveling salesman problem
is NP-hard to solve exactly, although there is a (1 + рқңҖ)-factor approximation algorithm
with running polynomial time for any constant рқңҖ > 0 (Arora 1998).
Let
рқҗҝ рқ‘ӣ = рқҗҝ (рқ‘Ҙ 1 , . . . , рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘ӣ )

162

with i.i.d. рқ‘Ҙ 1 , . . . , рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘ӣ вҲј Unif([0, 1] 2 )

9.6 Euclidean traveling salesman problem

The Mona Lisa TSP challenge.

A tour of 1000 random points.

вҲҡ
Exercise: Eрқҗҝ рқ‘ӣ = Оҳ( рқ‘ӣ)
вҲҡ
Beardwood, Halton, and Hammersley (1959) showed that whp рқҗҝ рқ‘ӣ / рқ‘ӣ converges to
some constant as рқ‘ӣ вҶ’ вҲһ (the exact value of the constant is unknown).
We shall focus on the concentration of рқҗҝ рқ‘ӣ .
We will present two methods that illustrate different techniques from this chapter.

Martingale methods
The following simple monotonicity property will be important for us: for any рқ‘Ҷ and
рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ [0, 1] 2 ,
рқҗҝ (рқ‘Ҷ) вүӨ рқҗҝ (рқ‘Ҷ вҲӘ {рқ‘Ҙ}) вүӨ рқҗҝ(рқ‘Ҷ) + 2 dist(рқ‘Ҙ, рқ‘Ҷ).
Here is the justification for the second inequality. Let рқ‘Ұ be the closest point in рқ‘Ҷ to
рқ‘Ҙ. Consider a shortest tour through рқ‘Ҷ of length рқҗҝ(рқ‘Ҷ). Let us modify this tour by first
traversing through it, and when we hit рқ‘Ұ, we take a detour excursion from рқ‘Ұ to рқ‘Ҙ and
then back to рқ‘Ұ. The length of this tour, which contains рқ‘Ҷ вҲӘ {рқ‘Ҙ}, is рқҗҝ(рқ‘Ҷ) + 2 dist(рқ‘Ҙ, рқ‘Ҷ),
and thus the shortest tour through рқ‘Ҷ вҲӘ {рқ‘Ҙ} has length at most рқҗҝ (рқ‘Ҷ) + 2 dist(рқ‘Ҙ, рқ‘Ҷ).
If we simply apply the bounded difference inequality, we find that changing a single
вҲҡ
рқ‘Ҙрқ‘– might change рқҗҝ(рқ‘Ҙ1 , . . . , рқ‘Ҙ рқ‘ӣ ) by рқ‘Ӯ (1) in the worse case, and so рқҗҝ рқ‘ӣ is рқ‘Ӯ ( рқ‘ӣ)вҲҡ
subGaussian about its mean. This is a trivial result since рқҗҝ рқ‘ӣ is typically Оҳ( рқ‘ӣ).
To do better, we apply AzumaвҖҷs inequlality to the Doob martingale. The key observation is that the initially revealed points do not affect the conditional expectations by
much even in the worst case.

9 Concentration of Measure

Remark 9.6.4. Rhee (1991) showed that this tail bound is sharp.

The proof below, following Steele (1997), applies the вҖңspace-filling curve heuristic.вҖқ
A space-filling curve is a continuous surjection from [0, 1] to [0, 1] 2 . Peano (1890)
constructed the first space-filling curve. Hilbert (1891) constructed another spacefilling curve known as the Hilbert curve. We will not give a precise description of the
Hilbert curve here. Intuitively, the Hilbert curve is the pointwise limit of a sequence of
piecewise linear curves illustrated in Figure 9.2. I recommend this 3Blue1Brown video
on YouTube for a beautiful animation of the Hilbert curve along with applications.
We will only need the following property of the Hilbert space filling curve.

165

9 Concentration of Measure

Figure 9.2: The Hilbert space-filling curve is the limit of discrete curves illustrated.

Definition 9.6.5 (HГ¶lder continuity)

Given two metric spaces (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘‘ рқ‘Ӣ ) and (рқ‘Ң , рқ‘‘рқ‘Ң ), we say that a map рқ‘“ : рқ‘Ӣ вҶ’ рқ‘Ң is HГ¶lder
continuous with exponent рқң¶ if there is some constant рқҗ¶ (depending on рқ‘“ ) so that
рқ‘‘рқ‘Ң ( рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ), рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ вҖІ)) вүӨ рқҗ¶рқ‘‘ рқ‘Ӣ (рқ‘Ҙ, рқ‘Ҙ вҖІ) рқӣј

for all рқ‘Ҙ, рқ‘Ҙ вҖІ вҲҲ рқ‘Ӣ.

Remark 9.6.6. HГ¶lder continuity with exponent 1 is the same as Lipschitz continuity.

Often рқ‘Ӣ has bounded diameter, in which case if рқ‘“ is HГ¶lder continuous with exponent
рқӣј, then it is so with any exponent рқӣјвҖІ < рқӣј.
Theorem 9.6.7

The Hilbert curve рқҗ» : [0, 1] вҶ’ [0, 1] 2 is HГ¶lder continuous with exponent 1/2.
Proof sketch. The Hilbert space-filling curve рқҗ» sends every interval of the form

[(рқ‘– вҲ’ 1)/4рқ‘ӣ , рқ‘–/4рқ‘ӣ ] to a square of the form [( рқ‘— вҲ’ 1)/2рқ‘ӣ , рқ‘—/2рқ‘ӣ ] Г— [(рқ‘ҳ вҲ’ 1)/2рқ‘ӣ , рқ‘ҳ/2рқ‘ӣ ].
Indeed, for each fixed рқ‘ӣ, the discrete curves eventually all have this property.
Let рқ‘Ҙ, рқ‘Ұ вҲҲ [0, 1], and let рқ‘ӣ be the largest integer so that рқ‘Ҙ, рқ‘Ұ вҲҲ [(рқ‘– вҲ’ 1)/4рқ‘ӣ , (рқ‘– +
1)/4рқ‘ӣ ] for some integer рқ‘–. Then |рқ‘Ҙ вҲ’ рқ‘Ұ| = Оҳ(4вҲ’рқ‘ӣ ), and |рқҗ» (рқ‘Ҙ) вҲ’ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ұ)| вүІ 2вҲ’рқ‘ӣ . Thus
|рқҗ» (рқ‘Ҙ) вҲ’ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ұ)| вүІ |рқ‘Ҙ вҲ’ рқ‘Ұ| 1/2 .

10 Entropy
My greatest concern was what to call it. I thought of calling it вҖңinformation,вҖқ but the word was overly used, so I decided to call it вҖңuncertainty.вҖқ
When I discussed it with John von Neumann, he had a better idea. Von
Neumann told me, вҖңYou should call it entropy, for two reasons. In the
first place your uncertainty function has been used in statistical mechanics
under that name, so it already has a name. In the second place, and more
important, nobody knows what entropy really is, so in a debate you will
always have the advantage.вҖқ
Claude Shannon, 1971
In this chapter, we look at some neat and powerful applications of entropy to combinatorics. For a standard introduction to information theory, see the textbook by Cover
and Thomas.

10.1 Basic properties
We define the (binary) entropy of a discrete random variable as follows.
Definition 10.1.1

Given a discrete random variable рқ‘Ӣ taking values in рқ‘Ҷ, with рқ‘қ рқ‘  := P(рқ‘Ӣ = рқ‘ ), its entropy
(or binary entropy to emphasis the base-2 logarithm) is defined to be
вҲ‘пёҒ
рқ‘Ҝ(рқ‘ҝ) :=
вҲ’рқ‘қ рқ‘  log2 рқ‘қ рқ‘ 
рқ‘ вҲҲрқ‘Ҷ

(by convention if рқ‘қ рқ‘  = 0 then the corresponding summand is set to zero).
Remark 10.1.2 (Base of the logarithm). It is also fine to use another base for the

logarithm, e.g., the natural log, as long as we are consistent throughout. There is some
combinatorial preference for base-2 due to its interpretation as counts bits. For certain
results, such as PinskerвҖҷs inequality (which we will unfortunately not cover here), the
choice of the base does matter.

173

10 Entropy
Remark 10.1.3 (Information theoretic interpretation). Intuitively, рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ) measures

the amount of вҖңsurpriseвҖқ in the randomness of рқ‘Ӣ. It can also be interpreted as the
amount of information learned by seeing the random variable рқ‘Ӣ. A more rigorous
interpretation of this intuition is given by the Shannon source coding theorem, which,
informally, says that the minimum number of bits needed to encode рқ‘ӣ iid copies of рқ‘Ӣ
is рқ‘ӣрқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ) + рқ‘ң(рқ‘ӣ).
Here are some basic properties. Throughout we only consider discrete random variables.
The proofs are all routine calculations. It will useful to understand the information
theoretic interpretations of these properties.
Lemma 10.1.4 (Uniform bound)

рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ) вүӨ log2 | support(рқ‘Ӣ)|,
with equality if and only if рқ‘Ӣ is uniformly distributed.
Proof. Let function рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ҙ) = вҲ’рқ‘Ҙ log2 рқ‘Ҙ is concave for рқ‘Ҙ вҲҲ [0, 1]. Let рқ‘Ҷ = support(рқ‘Ӣ).

Intuitively, the conditional entropy рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Ң ) measures the amount of additional information in рқ‘Ӣ not contained in рқ‘Ң . This is intuition is also captured by the next

Some important special cases:
вҖў If рқ‘Ӣ = рқ‘Ң , or рқ‘Ӣ = рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ң ), then рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Ң ) = 0.
вҖў If рқ‘Ӣ and рқ‘Ң are independent, then рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Ң ) = рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ)
вҖў If рқ‘Ӣ and рқ‘Ң are conditionally independent on рқ‘Қ, then рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң |рқ‘Қ) = рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Қ) +
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң |рқ‘Қ) and рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Ң , рқ‘Қ) = рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Қ).

рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң ) = рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң |рқ‘Ӣ)

Remark 10.1.9 (Mutual information). The nonnegative quantity

рқҗј (рқ‘Ӣ; рқ‘Ң ) := рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң ) вҲ’ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң )
is called mutual information. Intuitively, it measures the amount of common information between рқ‘Ӣ and рқ‘Ң .

Lemma 10.1.10 (Dropping conditioning)

рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Ң ) вүӨ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ) and more generally,
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Ң , рқ‘Қ) вүӨ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Қ).
Proof. By chain rule and subadditivity, we have

рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Ң ) = рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң ) вҲ’ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң ) вүӨ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ).
The inequality conditioning on рқ‘Қ follows since the above implies that
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Ң , рқ‘Қ = рқ‘§) вүҘ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Қ = рқ‘§)
holds for every рқ‘§, and taking expectation of рқ‘§ yields рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Ң , рқ‘Қ) вүӨ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Қ).

Remark 10.1.11. A related theorem is the data processing inequality: рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ | рқ‘“ (рқ‘Ң )) вүҘ

рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Ң ) for any function рқ‘“ . More generally, рқ‘“ can be random. In other words, if
рқ‘Ӣ вҶ’ рқ‘Ң вҶ’ рқ‘Қ is a Markov chain, then рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Қ) вүҘ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ |рқ‘Ң ) (exercise: prove this).

WeвҖҷll consider {0, 1}-valued matrices. If рқҗҙ is the bipartite adjacency matrix of a
bipartite graph, then

The following theorem gives an upper bound on the number of perfect matchings of
a bipartite graph with a given degree distribution. It was conjectured by Minc (1963)
and proved by BrГ©gman (1973).
Theorem 10.2.1 (BrГ©gmanвҖ“Minc inequality)

Let рқҗҙ = (рқ‘Һрқ‘– рқ‘— ) вҲҲ {0, 1}рқ‘ӣГ—рқ‘ӣ , whose рқ‘–-th row has sum рқ‘‘рқ‘– . Then

(рқ‘‘рқ‘– !) 1/рқ‘‘рқ‘–

рқ‘–=1

Note that equality is attained when рқҗҙ consists diagonal blocks of 1вҖҷs (corresponding
to perfect matchings in a bipartite graph of the form рқҗҫ рқ‘‘1 ,рқ‘‘1 вҠ” В· В· В· вҠ” рқҗҫ рқ‘‘рқ‘Ў ,рқ‘‘рқ‘Ў ).

Proof. (Radhakrishnan 1997) Let рқңҺ be as earlier. Consider a permutation of рқңҸ repre-

10.2 Permanent, perfect matchings, and Steiner triple systems

The maximum number of Hamilton paths in a tournament
Question 10.2.3

What is the maximum possible number of directed Hamilton paths in an рқ‘ӣ-vertex
tournament?
Earlier we saw that a uniformly random tournament has рқ‘ӣ!/2рқ‘ӣвҲ’1 Hamilton paths in
expectation, and hence there is some tournament with at least this many Hamilton
paths. This result, due to Szele, is the earliest application of the probabilistic method.
Using BrГ©gmanвҖҷs theorem, Alon proved a nearly matching upper bound.
Theorem 10.2.4 (Alon 1990)

Every рқ‘ӣ-vertex tournament has at most рқ‘Ӯ (рқ‘ӣ3/2 В· рқ‘ӣ!/2рқ‘ӣ ) Hamilton paths.
Remark 10.2.5. The upper bound has been improved to рқ‘Ӯ (рқ‘ӣ3/2вҲ’рқӣҫ рқ‘ӣ!/2рқ‘ӣ ) for some

small constant рқӣҫ > 0 (Friedgut and Kahn 2005), while the lower bound рқ‘ӣ!/2рқ‘ӣвҲ’1 has
been improved by a constant factor (Adler, Alon, and Ross 2001, Wormald 2004). It
remains open to close this рқ‘ӣрқ‘Ӯ (1) factor gap.
We first prove an upper bound on the number of Hamilton cycles.
Theorem 10.2.6 (Alon 1990)

вҲҡ
Every рқ‘ӣ-vertex tournament has at most рқ‘Ӯ ( рқ‘ӣ В· рқ‘ӣ!/2рқ‘ӣ ) Hamilton cycles.

Proof. Let рқҗҙ be an рқ‘ӣ Г— рқ‘ӣ matrix whose (рқ‘–, рқ‘—) entry is 1 if рқ‘– вҶ’ рқ‘— is an edge of the

tournament and 0 otherwise. Let рқ‘‘рқ‘– be the sum of the рқ‘–-th row. Then per рқҗҙ counts the
number of 1-factors (spanning disjoint unions of directed cycles) of the tournament.
So by BrГ©gmanвҖҷs theorem, we have
number of Hamilton cycles вүӨ per рқҗҙ вүӨ

Theorem 10.2.4 then follows by applying the above bound with the following lemma.

181

10 Entropy

Lemma 10.2.7

Given an рқ‘ӣ-vertex tournament with рқ‘ғ Hamilton paths, one can add a new vertex to
obtain a (рқ‘ӣ + 1)-vertex tournament with at least рқ‘ғ/4 Hamilton cycles.
Proof. Add a new vertex and orient its incident edges uniformly at random. For every

Hamilton path in the рқ‘ӣ-vertex tournament, there is probability 1/4 that it can be closed
up into a Hamilton cycle through the new vertex. The claim then follows by linearity
of expectation.
в–Ў

Steiner triple systems
Definition 10.2.8 (Steiner triple system)

A Steiner triple system (STS) of order рқ‘ӣ is a 3-uniform hypergraph on рқ‘ӣ vertices where
every pair of vertices is contained in exactly one triple.
Equivalently: an STS is a decomposition of a complete graph рқҗҫрқ‘ӣ into edge-disjoint
triangles.
Example: the Fano plane is an STS of order 7.
It is a classic result that an STS of order рқ‘ӣ exists if and only if рқ‘ӣ вүЎ 1 or 3 mod 6. It is

not hard to see that this is necessary, since if an STS of order рқ‘ӣ exsits, then рқ‘ӣ2 should
be divisible by 3, and рқ‘ӣ вҲ’ 1 should be divisible by 2. Keevash (2014+) obtained a
significant breakthrough proving the existence of more general designs.
Question 10.2.9

How many STS are there on рқ‘ӣ labeled vertices?
We shall prove the following result.
Theorem 10.2.10 (Upper bound on the number of STS вҖ” Linial and Luria 2013)

The number of Steiner triple systems on рқ‘ӣ labeled vertices is at most

(mod 6).
