10.3 SidorenkoвҖҷs inequality
Given graphs рқҗ№ and рқҗә, a graph homomorphism from рқҗ№ to рқҗә is a map рқңҷ : рқ‘ү (рқҗ№) вҶ’
рқ‘ү (рқҗә) of vertices that sends edges to edges, i.e., рқңҷ(рқ‘ў)рқңҷ(рқ‘Ј) вҲҲ рқҗё (рқҗә) for all рқ‘ўрқ‘Ј вҲҲ рқҗё (рқҗ№).
Let
hom(рқҗ№, рқҗә) = the number of graph homomorphisms from рқҗ№ to рқҗә.
Define the homomorphism density (the рқ‘Ҝ-density in рқ‘®) by
hom(рқҗ№, рқҗә)
рқ‘Ј(рқҗә) рқ‘Ј(рқҗ№)
= P(a uniform random map рқ‘ү (рқҗ№) вҶ’ рқ‘ү (рқҗә) is a graph homomorphism рқҗ№ вҶ’ рқҗә)

рқ‘Ў (рқҗ№, рқҗ») =

In this section, we are interested in the regime of fixed рқҗ№ and large рқҗә, in which case
almost all maps рқ‘ү (рқҗ№) вҶ’ рқ‘ү (рқҗә) are injective, so that there is not much difference
between homomorphisms and subgraphs. More precisely,
hom(рқҗ№, рқҗә) = aut(рқҗ№)(#copies of рқҗ№ in рқҗә as a subgraph) + рқ‘Ӯ рқҗ№ (рқ‘Ј(рқҗә) рқ‘Ј(рқҗ№)вҲ’1 ).
where aut(рқҗ№) is the number of automorphisms of рқҗ№.
Inequalities between graph homomorphism densities is a central topic in extremal
graph theory. For example, see Chapter 5 of my book Graph Theory and Additive
Combinatorics. Much of the rest of this chapter is adapted from В§5.5 of the book.
Question 10.3.1

Given a fixed graph рқҗ№ and constant рқ‘қ вҲҲ [0, 1], what is the minimum possible рқҗ№-density
in a graph with edge density at least рқ‘қ?

185

10 Entropy
The рқҗ№-density in the random graph рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, рқ‘қ) is рқ‘қ рқ‘’(рқҗ№) +рқ‘ң(1). Here рқ‘қ is fixed and рқ‘ӣ вҶ’ вҲһ.
Can one do better?
If рқҗ№ is non-bipartite, then the complete bipartite graph рқҗҫрқ‘ӣ/2,рқ‘ӣ/2 has рқҗ№-density zero.
(The problem of minimizing рқҗ№-density is still interesting and not easy; it has been
solved for cliques.)
SidorenkoвҖҷs conjecture (1993) (also proposed by ErdЕ‘s and Simonovits (1983)) says
for any fixed bipartite рқҗ№, the random graph asymptotically minimizes рқҗ№-density. This
is an important and well-known conjecture in extremal graph theory.
Conjecture 10.3.2 (Sidorenko)

For every bipartite graph рқҗ№, and any graph рқҗә,
рқ‘Ў (рқҗ№, рқҗә) вүҘ рқ‘Ў (рқҗҫ2 , рқҗә) рқ‘’(рқҗ№) .
The conjecture is known to hold for a large family of graphs рқҗ№.
The entropy approach to SidorenkoвҖҷs conjecture was first introduced by Li and Szegedy
(2011) and later further developed in subsequent works. Here we illustrate the entropy
approach to SidorenkoвҖҷs conjecture with several examples.
We will construct a probability distribution рқңҮ on Hom(рқҗ№, рқҗә), the set of all graph
homomorphisms рқҗ№ вҶ’ рқҗә. Unlike earlier applications of entropy, here we are trying to
prove a lower bound on hom(рқҗ№, рқҗә) instead of an upper bound. So instead of taking
рқңҮ to be a uniform distribution (which automatically has entropy log2 hom(рқҗ№, рқҗә)), we
actually take рқңҮ to be carefully constructed distribution, and apply the upper bound
рқҗ» (рқңҮ) вүӨ log2 |support рқңҮ| = log2 hom(рқҗ№, рқҗә).
We are trying to show that


2рқ‘’(рқҗә)
hom(рқҗ№, рқҗә)
.
вүҘ
рқ‘Ј(рқҗә) 2
рқ‘Ј(рқҗә) рқ‘Ј(рқҗ№)
So we would like to find a probability distribution рқңҮ on Hom(рқҗ№, рқҗә) satisfying
рқҗ» (рқңҮ) вүҘ рқ‘’(рқҗ№) log2 (2рқ‘’(рқҗә)) вҲ’ (2рқ‘’(рқҗ№) вҲ’ рқ‘Ј(рқҗ№)) log2 рқ‘Ј(рқҗә).

Theorem 10.3.3 (Blakey and Roy 1965)

SidorenkoвҖҷs conjecture holds if рқҗ№ is a three-edge path.
Proof. We choose randomly a walk рқ‘Ӣрқ‘Ң рқ‘Қрқ‘Ҡ in рқҗә as follows:

186

(10.1)

10.3 SidorenkoвҖҷs inequality
вҖў рқ‘Ӣрқ‘Ң is a uniform random edge of рқҗә (by this we mean first choosing an edge of
рқҗә uniformly at random, and then let рқ‘Ӣ be a uniformly chosen endpoint of this
edge, and then рқ‘Ң the other endpoint);
вҖў рқ‘Қ is a uniform random neighbor of рқ‘Ң ;
вҖў рқ‘Ҡ is a uniform random neighbor of рқ‘Қ.
Key observation: рқ‘Ң рқ‘Қ is distributed as a uniform random edge of рқҗә, and likewise with
рқ‘Қрқ‘Ҡ
Indeed, conditioned on the choice of рқ‘Ң , the vertices рқ‘Ӣ and рқ‘Қ are both independent and
uniform neighbors of рқ‘Ң , so рқ‘Ӣрқ‘Ң and рқ‘Ң рқ‘Қ are uniformly distributed.
Also, the conditional independence observation implies that
рқҗ» (рқ‘Қ |рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң ) = рқҗ» (рқ‘Қ |рқ‘Ң )

and

рқҗ» (рқ‘Ҡ |рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң , рқ‘Қ) = рқҗ» (рқ‘Ҡ |рқ‘Қ)

and futhermore both quantities are equal to рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң |рқ‘Ӣ) since рқ‘Ӣрқ‘Ң , рқ‘Ң рқ‘Қ, рқ‘Қрқ‘Ҡ are each distributed as a uniform random edge.
Thus
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң , рқ‘Қ, рқ‘Ҡ) = рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң |рқ‘Ӣ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Қ |рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ҡ |рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң , рқ‘Қ)
= рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң |рқ‘Ӣ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Қ |рқ‘Ң ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ҡ |рқ‘Қ)

[chain rule]
[cond indep]

= рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ) + 3рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң |рқ‘Ӣ)
= 3рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң ) вҲ’ 2рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ)

[chain rule]

вүҘ 3 log2 (2рқ‘’(рқҗә)) вҲ’ 2 log2 рқ‘Ј(рқҗә)
In the final step we used рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң ) = log2 (2рқ‘’(рқҗә)) since рқ‘Ӣрқ‘Ң is uniformly distributed
among edges, and рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ) вүӨ log2 |support(рқ‘Ӣ)| = log2 рқ‘Ј(рқҗә). This proves (10.1) and
hence the theorem for a path of 4 vertices. (As long as the final expression has the
вҖңright formвҖқ and none of the steps are lossy, the proof should work out.)

proofs.
The above proof easily generalizes to all trees. We omit the details.

Theorem 10.3.6

SidorenkoвҖҷs conjecture holds for all complete bipartite graphs.
Proof. Following the same framework as earlier, let us demonstrate the result for

рқҗ№ = рқҗҫ2,2 . The same proof extends to all рқҗҫ рқ‘ ,рқ‘Ў .
рқ‘Ҙ2

рқ‘Ұ2

рқ‘Ҙ1

рқ‘Ұ1

We will pick a random tuple (рқ‘Ӣ1 , рқ‘Ӣ2 , рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 ) вҲҲ рқ‘ү (рқҗә) 4 with рқ‘Ӣрқ‘–рқ‘Ң рқ‘— вҲҲ рқҗё (рқҗә) for all рқ‘–, рқ‘— as
follows.
вҖў рқ‘Ӣ1рқ‘Ң1 is a uniform random edge;
вҖў рқ‘Ң2 is a uniform random neighbor of рқ‘Ӣ1 ;
вҖў рқ‘Ӣ2 is a conditionally independent copy of рқ‘Ӣ1 given (рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 ).
The last point deserves more attention. Note that we are not simply uniformly randomly
choosing a common neighbor of рқ‘Ң1 and рқ‘Ң2 as one might naively attempt. Instead, one
can think of the first two steps as generating a distribution for (рқ‘Ӣ1 , рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 )вҖ”according to
this distribution, we first generate (рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 ) according to its marginal, and then produce
two conditionally independent copies of рқ‘Ӣ1 (the second copy is рқ‘Ӣ2 ).
As in the previous proof (applied to a 2-edge path), we see that
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ1 , рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 ) = 2рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ1 , рқ‘Ң1 ) вҲ’ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ1 ) вүҘ 2 log2 (2рқ‘’(рқҗә)) вҲ’ log2 рқ‘Ј(рқҗә).
So we have
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ1 , рқ‘Ӣ2 , рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 )
= рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ1 , рқ‘Ӣ2 |рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 )

[chain rule]

= рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 ) + 2рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ1 |рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 )

[conditional independence]

= 2рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ1 , рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 ) вҲ’ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 )

[chain rule]

вүҘ 2(2 log2 (2рқ‘’(рқҗә)) вҲ’ log2 рқ‘Ј(рқҗә)) вҲ’ 2 log2 рқ‘Ј(рқҗә).

[prev. ineq. and uniform bound]

= 4 log(2рқ‘’(рқҗә)) вҲ’ 4 log2 рқ‘Ј(рқҗә).
So we have verified (10.1) for рқҗҫ2,2 .

Theorem 10.3.7 (Conlon, Fox, Sudakov 2010)

SidorenkoвҖҷs conjecture holds for a bipartite graph that has a vertex adjacent to all
vertices in the other part.
Proof. Let us illustrate the proof for the following graph. The proof extends to the

general case.
рқ‘Ұ1
рқ‘Ҙ1
рқ‘Ҙ0
рқ‘Ұ2

рқ‘Ҙ2

рқ‘Ұ3
Let us choose a random tuple (рқ‘Ӣ0 , рқ‘Ӣ1 , рқ‘Ӣ2 , рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 ) вҲҲ рқ‘ү (рқҗә) 6 as follows:
вҖў рқ‘Ӣ0рқ‘Ң1 is a uniform random edge;
вҖў рқ‘Ң2 and рқ‘Ң3 are independent uniform random neighbors of рқ‘Ӣ0 ;
вҖў рқ‘Ӣ1 is a conditionally independent copy of рқ‘Ӣ0 given (рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 );
вҖў рқ‘Ӣ2 is a conditionally independent copy of рқ‘Ӣ0 given (рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 ).
(as well as other symmetric versions.) Some important properties of this distribution:
вҖў рқ‘Ӣ0 , рқ‘Ӣ1 , рқ‘Ӣ2 are conditionally independent given (рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 );
вҖў рқ‘Ӣ1 and (рқ‘Ӣ0 , рқ‘Ң3 , рқ‘Ӣ2 ) are conditionally independent given (рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 );
вҖў The distribution of (рқ‘Ӣ0 , рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 ) is identical to the distribution of (рқ‘Ӣ1 , рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 ).
We have
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ0 , рқ‘Ӣ1 , рқ‘Ӣ2 , рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 )
= рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ0 , рқ‘Ӣ1 , рқ‘Ӣ2 |рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 )

[chain rule]

= рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ0 |рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ1 |рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ2 |рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 )

[cond indep]

= рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ0 |рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ1 |рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ2 |рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 )

[cond indep]

= рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ0 , рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ1 , рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ2 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 ) вҲ’ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 ) вҲ’ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 ). [chain rule]
The proof of Theorem 10.3.3 actually lower bounds the first three terms:
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ0 , рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 ) вүҘ 3 log2 (2рқ‘’(рқҗә)) вҲ’ 2 log2 рқ‘Ј(рқҗә)
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ1 , рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 ) вүҘ 2 log2 (2рқ‘’(рқҗә)) вҲ’ log2 рқ‘Ј(рқҗә)
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ2 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 ) вүҘ 2 log2 (2рқ‘’(рқҗә)) вҲ’ log2 рқ‘Ј(рқҗә).

189

10 Entropy
We can apply the uniform support bound on the remaining terms.
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 ) = рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 ) вүӨ 2 log2 рқ‘Ј(рқҗә).
Putting everything together, we have
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ0 , рқ‘Ӣ1 , рқ‘Ӣ2 , рқ‘Ң1 , рқ‘Ң2 , рқ‘Ң3 ) вүҘ 7 log2 (2рқ‘’(рқҗә)) вҲ’ 8 log2 рқ‘Ј(рқҗә),
thereby verifying (10.1).

Remark 10.3.8 (MГ¶bius graph). An important open case (and the smallest in some

sense) of Sidorenko conjecture is when рқҗ№ is the following graph, known as the MГ¶bius
graph. It is рқҗҫ5,5 with a 10-cycle removed. The name comes from it being the facevertex incidence graph of the simplicial complex structure of the MГ¶bius strip, built
by gluing a strip of five triangles.

10.4 ShearerвҖҷs lemma
ShearerвҖҷs entropy lemma extends the subadditivity property of entropy. Before stating
it in full generality, let us first see the simplest instance of ShearerвҖҷs lemma.
Theorem 10.4.1 (ShearerвҖҷs lemma, special case)

2рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң , рқ‘Қ) вүӨ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Қ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң , рқ‘Қ)
Proof. Using the chain rule and conditioning dropping, we have

рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң ) = рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң |рқ‘Ӣ)
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Қ) = рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ)
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң , рқ‘Қ) =

+ рқҗ» (рқ‘Қ |рқ‘Ӣ)
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Қ |рқ‘Ң )

вүҘ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ)
вүҘ

+ рқҗ» (рқ‘Қ |рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Қ)
рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң |рқ‘Ӣ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Қ |рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң )

Applying conditioning dropping, we see that their sum is at at least
2рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ) + 2рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң |рқ‘Ӣ) + 2рқҗ» (рқ‘Қ |рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң ) = 2рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң , рқ‘Қ).

Question 10.4.2

What is the maximum volume of a body in R3 that has area at most 1 when projected
to each of the three coordinate planes?
The cube [0, 1] 3 satisfies the above property and has area 1. It turns out that this is the
maximum.
To prove this claim, first let us use ShearerвҖҷs inequality to prove a discrete version.
Theorem 10.4.3

Let рқ‘Ҷ вҠҶ R3 be a finite set, and рқңӢрқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ұ (рқ‘Ҷ) be its projection on the рқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ұ-plane, etc. Then
|рқ‘Ҷ| 2 вүӨ рқңӢрқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ұ (рқ‘Ҷ) |рқңӢрқ‘Ҙрқ‘§ (рқ‘Ҷ)| рқңӢ рқ‘Ұрқ‘§ (рқ‘Ҷ)
Proof. Let (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң , рқ‘Қ) be a uniform random point of рқ‘Ҷ. Then

2 log2 |рқ‘Ҷ| = 2рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң , рқ‘Қ) вүӨ рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Ң ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ӣ, рқ‘Қ) + рқҗ» (рқ‘Ң , рқ‘Қ)
вүӨ log2 рқңӢрқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ұ (рқ‘Ҷ) + log2 рқңӢрқ‘Ҙрқ‘§ (рқ‘Ҷ) + log2 рқңӢ рқ‘Ұрқ‘§ (рқ‘Ҷ).

Triangle-intersecting families
We say that a set G of labeled graphs on the same vertex set is triangle-intersecting if
рқҗә вҲ© рқҗә вҖІ contains a triangle for every рқҗә, рқҗә вҖІ вҲҲ G.
Question 10.4.8

What is the largest triangle-intersecting family of graphs on рқ‘ӣ labeled vertices?
The set of all graphs that contain a fixed triangle is triangle-intersecting, and they form
a 1/8 fraction of all graphs.
An easy upper bound: the edges form an intersecting family, so a triangle-intersecting
family must be at most 1/2 fraction of all graphs.
The next theorem improves this upper bound to < 1/4. It is also in this paper that
ShearerвҖҷs lemma was introduced.
Theorem 10.4.9 (Chung, Graham, Frankl, and Shearer 1986)

Every triangle-intersecting family of graphs on рқ‘ӣ labeled vertices has size < 2 ( 2) вҲ’2 .

The number of independent sets in a regular bipartite graph
Question 10.4.11

Fix рқ‘‘. Which рқ‘‘-regular graph on a given number of vertices has the most number of
independent sets? Alternatively, which graph рқҗә maximizes рқ‘–(рқҗә) 1/рқ‘Ј(рқҗә) ?
(Note that the number of independent sets is multiplicative: рқ‘–(рқҗә 1 вҠ”рқҗә 2 ) = рқ‘–(рқҗә 1 )рқ‘–(рқҗә 2 ).)
Alon and Kahn conjectured that for graphs on рқ‘ӣ vertices, when рқ‘ӣ is a multiple of 2рқ‘‘,
a disjoint union of рқҗҫ рқ‘‘,рқ‘‘ вҖҷs maximizes the number of independent sets.

193

10 Entropy
Alon (1991) proved an approximate version of this conjecture. Kahn (2001) proved it
assuming the graph is bipartite. Zhao (2010) proved it in general.
Theorem 10.4.12 (Kahn, Zhao)

Let рқҗә be an рқ‘ӣ-vertex рқ‘‘-regular graph. Then

Now we give the argument from Zhao (2010) that removes the bipartite hypothesis.
The following combinatorial argument reduces the problem for non-bipartite рқҗә to that
of bipartite рқҗә.
Starting from a graph рқҗә, we construct its bipartite double cover рқҗә Г— рқҗҫ2 (see Figure 10.1), which has vertex set рқ‘ү (рқҗә) Г— {0, 1}. The vertices of рқҗә Г— рқҗҫ2 are labeled рқ‘Ј рқ‘–
for рқ‘Ј вҲҲ рқ‘ү (рқҗә) and рқ‘– вҲҲ {0, 1}. Its edges are рқ‘ў 0 рқ‘Ј 1 for all рқ‘ўрқ‘Ј вҲҲ рқҗё (рқҗә). Note that рқҗә Г— рқҗҫ2
is always a bipartite graph.
Lemma 10.4.13

Let рқҗә be any graph (not necessarily regular). Then
рқ‘–(рқҗә) 2 вүӨ рқ‘–(рқҗә Г— рқҗҫ2 ).

The entropy proof of the bipartite case of Theorem 10.4.12 extends to graph homomorphisms, yielding the following result.
Theorem 10.4.14 (Galvin and Tetali 2004)

Let рқҗә be an рқ‘ӣ-vertex рқ‘‘-regular bipartite graph. Let рқҗ» be any graph allowing loops.
Then
hom(рқҗә, рқҗ») вүӨ hom(рқҗҫ рқ‘‘,рқ‘‘ , рқҗ») рқ‘ӣ/(2рқ‘‘)
Some important special cases:
вҖў hom(рқҗә,

) = рқ‘–(рқҗә), the number of independent sets of рқҗә;

вҖў hom(рқҗә, рқҗҫрқ‘һ ) = the number of proper рқ‘һ-colorings of рқҗә.
The bipartite hypothesis in Theorem 10.4.14 cannot be always be removed. For
example, if рқҗ» =
, then log2 hom(рқҗә, рқҗ») is the number of connected components
of рқҗә, so that the maximizers of log2 hom(рқҗә, рқҗ»)/рқ‘Ј(рқҗә) are disjoint unions of рқҗҫ рқ‘‘+1 вҖҷs.
For рқҗ» = рқҗҫрқ‘һ , corresponding to the proper рқ‘һ-colorings, the bipartite hypothesis was
recently removed.
Theorem 10.4.15 (Sah, Sawhney, Stoner, and Zhao 2020)

Let рқҗә be an рқ‘ӣ-vertex рқ‘‘-regular graph. Then
рқ‘җ рқ‘һ (рқҗә) вүӨ рқ‘җ рқ‘һ (рқҗҫ рқ‘‘,рқ‘‘ ) рқ‘ӣ/(2рқ‘‘)
where рқ‘җ рқ‘һ (рқҗә) is the number of рқ‘һ-colorings of рқҗә.
Furthermore, it was also shown in the same paper that in Theorem 10.4.14, the bipartite
hypothesis on рқҗә can be weakened to triangle-free. Furthermore triangle-free is the
weakest possible hypothesis on рқҗә so that the claim is true for all рқҗ».
For more discussion and open problems on this topic, see the survey by Zhao (2017).

11 Containers
Many problems in combinatorics can be phrased in terms of independent sets in
hypergraphs.
For example, here is a model question:
Question 11.0.1

How many triangle-free graphs are there on рқ‘ӣ vertices?
2

By taking all subgraphs of рқҗҫрқ‘ӣ/2,рқ‘ӣ/2 , we obtain 2рқ‘ӣ /4 such graphs. It turns out this gives
the correct exponential asymptotic.
Theorem 11.0.2 (ErdЕ‘s, Kleitman, and Rothschild 1973)
2

2

The number of triangle-free graphs on рқ‘ӣ vertices is 2рқ‘ӣ /4+рқ‘ң(рқ‘ӣ ) .
Remark 11.0.3. It does not matter here whether we consider vertices to be labeled, it

affects the answer up to a factor of at most рқ‘ӣ! = рқ‘’рқ‘Ӯ (рқ‘ӣ log рқ‘ӣ) .
Remark 11.0.4. Actually the original ErdЕ‘sвҖ“KleitmanвҖ“Rothschild paper showed an

even stronger result: 1 вҲ’ рқ‘ң(1) fraction of all рқ‘ӣ-vertex triangle-free graphs are bipartite.
The above asymptotic can be then easily deduced by counting subgraphs of complete
bipartite graphs. The container methods discussed in this section are not strong enough
to prove this finer claim.
We can convert this asymptotic enumeration problem into a problem about independent
sets in a 3-uniform hypergraph рқҗ»:

вҖў рқ‘ү (рқҗ») = [рқ‘ӣ]
2
вҖў The edges of рқҗ» are triples of the form {рқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ұ, рқ‘Ҙрқ‘§, рқ‘Ұрқ‘Ҙ}, i.e., triangles
We then have the correspondence:
вҖў A subset of рқ‘ү (рқҗ») = a graph on vertex set [рқ‘ӣ]
вҖў An independent set of рқ‘ү (рқҗ») = a triangle-free graph

201

11 Containers
(Here an independent set in a hypergraph is a subset of vertices containing no edges.)
Naively applying first moment/union bound does not workвҖ”there are too many events
to union bound over.
For example, MantelвҖҷs theorem tell us the maximum number of edges in an рқ‘ӣ-vertex


triangle-free graph is рқ‘ӣ2 /4 , obtained by рқҗҫ вҢҠрқ‘ӣ/2вҢӢ,вҢҲрқ‘ӣ/2вҢү . With a fixed triangle-free graph
рқҗә, the number of subgraphs of рқҗә is 2рқ‘’(рқҗә) , and each of them is triangle-free. Perhaps
we could union bound over all maximal triangle-free graphs? It turns out that there are
2
2
2рқ‘ӣ /8+рқ‘ң(рқ‘ӣ ) such maximal triangle-free graphs, so a union bound would be too wasteful.
In many applications, independent sets are clustered into relatively few highly correlated sets. In the case of triangle-free graphs, each maximal triangle-free graph is very
вҖңcloseвҖқ to many other maximal triangle-free graphs.
Is there a more efficient union bound that takes account of the clustering of independent
sets?
The container method does exactly that. Given some hypergraph with controlled
degrees, one can find a collection of containers satisfying the following properties:
вҖў Each container is a subset of vertices of the hypergraph.
вҖў Every independent set of the hypergraph is a subset of some container.
вҖў The total number of containers in the collection is relatively small.
вҖў Each container is not too large (in fact, not too much larger than the maximum
size of an independent set)
We can then union bound over all such containers. If the number of containers is not
too small, then the union bound is not too lossy.
Here are some of the most typical and important applications of the container method:
вҖў Asymptotic enumerations:
вҖ“ Counting рқҗ»-free graphs on рқ‘ӣ vertices
вҖ“ Counting рқҗ»-free graphs on рқ‘ӣ vertices and рқ‘ҡ edges
вҖ“ Counting рқ‘ҳ-AP-free subsets of [рқ‘ӣ] of size рқ‘ҡ
вҖў Extremal and Ramsey results in random structures:
вҖ“ The maximum number of edges in an рқҗ»-free subgraph of рқҗә (рқ‘ӣ, рқ‘қ)
вҖ“ SzemeЕ•ediвҖҷs theorem in a рқ‘қ-random subset of [рқ‘ӣ]
вҖў List coloring in graphs/hypergraphs

202

11.1 Containers for triangle-free graphs
The method of hypergraph containers is one of the most exciting developments in this
past decade. Some references and further reading:
вҖў The graph container method was developed by Kleitman and Winston (1982) (for
counting рқҗ¶4 -free graphs) and Sapozhenko (2001) (for bounding the number of
independent sets in a regular graph, giving an earlier version of Theorem 10.4.12)
вҖў The hypergraph container theorem was proved independently by Balogh, Morris,
and SamotДі (2015), and Saxton and Thomason (2015).
вҖў See the 2018 ICM survey of Balogh, Morris, and SamotДі for an introduction to
the topic along with many applications
вҖў See SamotДівҖҷs survey article (2015) for an introduction to the graph container
method
вҖў See MorrisвҖҷ lecture notes (2016) for a gentle introduction to the proof and
applications of hypergraph containers.

11.2 Graph containers
Theorem 11.2.1 (Container theorem for independent sets in graphs)

For every рқ‘җ > 0, there exists рқӣҝ > 0 such that the following holds.
Let рқҗә = (рқ‘ү, рқҗё) be a graph with average degree рқ‘‘ and maximum degree at most рқ‘җрқ‘‘.
There exists a collection C of subsets of рқ‘ү, with


|рқ‘ү |
|C| вүӨ
вүӨ 2рқӣҝ |рқ‘ү | /рқ‘‘
such that
1. Every independent set рқҗј of рқҗә is contained in some рқҗ¶ вҲҲ C.
2. |рқҗ¶ | вүӨ (1 вҲ’ рқӣҝ) |рқ‘ү | for every рқҗ¶ вҲҲ C.
Each рқҗ¶ вҲҲ C is called a вҖңcontainer.вҖқ Every independent set of рқҗ¶ is contained in some
container.
Remark 11.2.2. The requirement |рқҗ¶ | вүӨ (1 вҲ’ рқӣҝ) |рқ‘ү | looks quite a bit weaker than

in Theorem 11.1.1, where each container is only slightly larger than the maximum
independent set. In a typical application of the container method, one iteratively applies
the (hyper)graph container theorem (e.g., Theorem 11.2.1 and later Theorem 11.3.1)
to the subgraphs induced by the slightly smaller containers in the previous iteration.
One iterates until the containers are close to their minimum possible size.
For this iterative application of container theorem to work, one usually needs a supersaturation result, which, roughly speaking, says that every subset of vertices that is
slightly larger than the independence number necessarily induces a lot of edges. This
property is common to all standard applications of the container method.
The container theorem is proved using
The graph container algorithm (for a fixed given graph рқҗә)
Input: a maximal independent set рқҗј вҠҶ рқ‘ү.
Output: a вҖңfingerprintвҖқ рқ‘Ҷ вҠҶ рқҗј of size вүӨ 2рқӣҝ |рқ‘ү | /рқ‘‘, and a container рқҗ¶ вҠҮ рқҗј which depends
only on рқ‘Ҷ.
Throughout the algorithm, we will maintain a partition рқ‘ү = рқҗҙ вҲӘ рқ‘Ҷ вҲӘ рқ‘Ӣ, where
вҖў рқҗҙ, the вҖңavailableвҖқ vertices, initially рқҗҙ = рқ‘ү
вҖў рқ‘Ҷ, the current fingerprint, initially рқ‘Ҷ = вҲ…
вҖў рқ‘Ӣ, the вҖңexcludedвҖқ vertices, initially рқ‘Ӣ = вҲ….

206

11.2 Graph containers
The max-degree order of рқҗә [ рқҗҙ] is an ordering of рқҗҙ in by the degree of the vertices
in рқҗә [ рқҗҙ], with the largest first, and breaking ties according to some arbitrary predetermined ordering of рқ‘ү.
While |рқ‘Ӣ | < рқӣҝ |рқ‘ү |:
1. Let рқ‘Ј be the first vertex of рқҗј вҲ© рқҗҙ in the max-degree order on рқҗә [ рқҗҙ].
2. Add рқ‘Ј to рқ‘Ҷ.
3. Add the neighbors of рқ‘Ј to рқ‘Ӣ.
4. Add vertices preceding рқ‘Ј in the max-degree order on рқҗә [ рқҗҙ] to рқ‘Ӣ.
5. Remove from рқҗҙ all the new vertices added to рқ‘Ҷ вҲӘ рқ‘Ӣ.
Claim: when the algorithm terminates, we obtain a partition рқ‘ү = рқҗҙ вҲӘ рқ‘Ҷ вҲӘ рқ‘Ӣ such that
|рқ‘Ӣ | вүҘ рқӣҝ |рқ‘ү | and |рқ‘Ҷ| вүӨ 2рқӣҝ |рқ‘ү | /рқ‘‘.
Proof idea: due to the degree hypotheses, in every iteration, at least вүҘ рқ‘‘/2 new vertices
are added to рқ‘Ӣ (provided that рқ‘‘ вүӨ 2рқӣҝ |рқ‘ү |). See MorrisвҖҷ lecture notes for details.
Key facts:
вҖў Two different maximal independent sets рқҗј, рқҗј вҖІ вҠҶ рқ‘ү that produce the same fingerprint рқ‘Ҷ in the algorithm necessarily produces the same partition рқ‘ү = рқҗҙ вҲӘ рқ‘Ҷ вҲӘ рқ‘Ӣ
вҖў The final set рқ‘Ҷ вҲӘ рқҗҙ contains рқҗј (since only vertices not in рқҗј are ever moved to рқҗј)
Therefore, the total number possibilities for containers рқ‘Ҷ вҲӘ рқҗҙ is at most the number of
sets рқ‘Ҷ вҠҶ рқ‘ү. Since |рқ‘Ҷ| вүӨ 2рқӣҝ |рқ‘ү | /рқ‘‘ and | рқҗҙ вҲӘ рқ‘Ҷ| вүӨ (1 вҲ’ рқӣҝ) |рқ‘ү |, this concludes the proof
of the graph container lemma.
The fingerprint obtained by the proof actually gives us a stronger consequence that
will be important for some applications.

вҖў рқ‘Ҷ(рқҗј) вҠҶ рқҗј вҠҶ рқ‘Ҷ(рқҗј) вҲӘ рқҗҙ(рқ‘Ҷ(рқҗј))

An independent set in a hypergraph is a subset of vertices containing no edges.

11.3 Hypergraph container theorem
Like the graph container theorem, the hypergraph container theorem is proved by
designing an algorithm to produce, from an independent set рқҗј вҠҶ рқ‘ү (рқҗ»), a fingerprint
рқ‘Ҷ вҠҶ рқҗј and a container рқҗ¶ вҠғ рқҗј.
The hypergraph container algorithm is more involved compared to the graph container
algorithm. In fact, the 3-uniform hypergraph container algorithm calls the graph
container algorithm.
Container algorithm for 3-uniform hypergraphs (a very rough sketch):
Throughout the algorithm, we will maintain
вҖў A fingerprint рқ‘Ҷ, initially рқ‘Ҷ = вҲ…
вҖў A 3-uniform hypergraph рқҗҙ, initially рқҗҙ = рқҗ»
вҖў A graph рқҗә of вҖңforbiddenвҖқ pairs on рқ‘ү (рқҗ»), initially рқҗә = вҲ…
вҲҡ
While |рқ‘Ҷ| вүӨ рқ‘Ј(рқҗ»)/ рқ‘‘ вҲ’ 1:
вҖў Let рқ‘ў be the first vertex in рқҗј in the max-degree order on рқҗҙ
вҖў Add рқ‘ў to рқ‘Ҷ
вҖў Add рқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ұ to рқҗё (рқҗә) whenever рқ‘ўрқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ұ вҲҲ рқҗё (рқҗ»)
вҖў Remove from рқ‘ү ( рқҗҙ) the vertex рқ‘ў as well as all vertices proceeding рқ‘ў in the
max-degree order on рқҗҙ
вҲҡ
вҖў Remove from рқ‘ү ( рқҗҙ) every vertex whose degree in рқҗә is larger than рқ‘җ рқ‘‘.
вҖў Remove from рқҗё ( рқҗҙ) every edge that contains an edge of рқҗә.
Finally, it is will be the case that either
вҖў We have removed many vertices from рқ‘ү ( рқҗҙ)
вҲҡ
вҲҡ
вҖў Or the final graph рқҗә has at least О©( рқ‘‘рқ‘ӣ) edges and has maximum degree рқ‘Ӯ ( рқ‘‘),
so that we can apply the graph container lemma to рқҗә.
In either case, the algorithm produces a container with the desired properties. Again
see MorrisвҖҷ lecture notes for details.
